Dialectic -- Jadal
beginner
5 min
The Quranic Roots and Scholarly Application of Jadal
Introduction explaining the significance of jadal as a method for debate in Islam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the dual role of jadal as derived from the Quran and its application in Islamic scholarly tradition.

Core Idea
Jadal is not mere argumentation but a Quranic method for refuting falsehood and convincing hearts.

This opening passage establishes the importance of jadal in Islam. The author emphasizes that jadal is not a later innovation but was used from the very beginning of the Prophet's mission. The Quran employed it both defensively (against opponents) and offensively (to attract seekers of truth). Muslim scholars later formalized it into an art for internal scholarly debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic usage
Note how the author says the Quran used jadal 'as a means to refute opponents' and 'to convince those ready to accept.' This shows the dual purpose.
The author explicitly mentions these two purposes in the same sentence.
2
Recognize the expansion into an art
The author states that scholars turned jadal into a 'صناعة' (art) for discussing issues and exchanging opinions to reach the truth.
This indicates a formalization of the method.
3
Observe the scope across Islamic sciences
The author lists creed, fiqh, usul, tafsir, and hadith as fields where jadal was applied. This shows its broad relevance.
Jadal was not limited to theology but permeated all Islamic disciplines.
4
Contextualize the evidence of jadal practice
The author points to scholarly works full of 'dialectical style' and to live debates in study circles, mosques, and rulers' councils as evidence.
Both written and oral traditions preserved jadal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحمد لله رب العالمين والصلاة والسلام على أشرف المرسلين سيدنا ونبينا محمد وعلى آله وصحبه أجمعين والتابعين ومن تبع هداهم بإحسان إلى يوم والعاقبة للمتقين، أما بعد: فيعتبر موضوع الجدل واحدا من أهم الموضوعات وأكثرها أحقية بالدراسة والبحث، فهو موضوع يتناول منهجًا ارتبط بالعقيدة الإسلامية من أول يوم أرسل ببيانها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، إذ اتخذ منه القرآن الكريم وسيلة إلى إفحام الخصوم الرافضين للعقيدة الإسلامية من جهة ووسيلة إلى إقناع أولئك الذين يتوفر لديهم الاستعداد لتقبل هذه العقيدة والحرص على فهم عناصرها من جهة ثانية. وقد استفاد العلماء المسلمون من توجيهات القرآن الكريم وأساليبه الحكيمة في هذا المجال، فاتخذوا من الجدل وسيلة إلى إقناع مخالفيهم في الرأي حتى تحول لديهم إلى صناعة يلجئون إليها إذا ما أرادوا تدارس المسائل وتقليب وجهات النظر وتبادل الرأي فيها حتى يتم الاستقرار على رأي أقرب إلى الصواب في شأنها. فلم يكن الجدل وسيلة إلى إفحام وإقناع مخالفي العقيدة الإسلامية فحسب، بل كان وسيلة كذلك إلى مناقشة وإقناع المسلمين فيما بينهم، وخاصة في الشئون والآراء العلمية المتعلقة بالعقيدة وفروع الفقه وأصوله ومسائل التفسير والحديث، وغيرها من القضايا التي تشغل الفكر الإسلامي. وذلك ما يظهر من خلال الرجوع إلى مؤلفات العلماء المسلمين في سائر علوم الشريعة الإسلامية المتنوعة عبر التاريخ الإسلامي الطويل، حيث نجدها حافلة بالمسائل الخلافية التي يسوقونها في طابع جدلي بحت يعتمد على إيراد الرأي والرأي المخالف وعرض أدلة كل رأي ومناقشتها مناقشة هادئة هادفة . وليست الكتب وحدها الميدان الذي عرف الجدل، فإن تاريخ العلوم في ظل الإسلام يشهد بأن دور العلم وحلقات المساجد ومجالس الحكام كانت قد شهدت الآلاف من المناظرات بين العلماء المسلمين فيما بينهم، أو بينهم وبين غيرهم من علماء الأديان الأخرى، حول مسائل علمية متنوعة بين عقدية وفقهية وأصولية
Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds, and blessings and peace be upon the most honorable of messengers, our master and prophet Muhammad, and upon his family and companions altogether, and the followers, and those who follow their guidance in righteousness until the Day of Judgment, and the end is for the righteous. To proceed: The subject of jadal is considered one of the most important subjects and most deserving of study and research. It is a subject that deals with a method that has been linked to the Islamic creed from the first day the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, was sent to explain it. The Holy Quran adopted it as a means to refute opponents rejecting the Islamic creed on one hand, and as a means to convince those who have the readiness to accept this creed and are keen to understand its elements on the other hand. Muslim scholars benefited from the directions of the Holy Quran and its wise methods in this field, so they adopted jadal as a means to convince their opponents in opinion, until it turned into an art they resort to whenever they want to discuss issues, turn over viewpoints, and exchange opinions until they settle on an opinion closer to the truth concerning it. For jadal was not only a means to refute and convince opponents of the Islamic creed, but it was also a means to discuss and convince among Muslims themselves, especially in scientific matters and opinions related to creed, branches of fiqh and its principles, issues of tafsir and hadith, and other issues that occupy Islamic thought. This is evident from referring to the works of Muslim scholars in all diverse Islamic sciences throughout long Islamic history, where we find them full of controversial issues presented in a purely dialectical style based on presenting the opinion and the opposing opinion, presenting the evidence for each opinion, and discussing them in a calm and purposeful discussion. Not only books are the field that knew jadal, for the history of sciences under Islam testifies that study circles, mosque study groups, and rulers' councils witnessed thousands of debates among Muslim scholars themselves, or between them and scholars of other religions, on various scientific issues, both creedal, jurisprudential, and usuli.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the introduction to the book 'Jadal Usuliyyin'. The author begins with the basmala and praise, then states the importance of the subject of jadal. He explains that jadal (dialectical debate) is a method rooted in the Islamic creed from the very beginning of the Prophet's mission. The Quran used it both to refute those who rejected Islam and to convince those open to the faith. Muslim scholars later adopted this method for internal scholarly discussions across all Islamic sciences, including creed, jurisprudence, principles of jurisprudence, exegesis, and hadith. The author emphasizes that jadal became a refined art (صناعة) used to examine issues, weigh arguments, and arrive at the soundest opinion. He notes that jadal was not limited to confronting non-Muslims but was also a tool for internal Muslim scholarly debate. The evidence from Islamic scholarly works shows a prevalence of dialectical engagement. Moreover, the practice extended beyond books into live debates in study circles, mosque gatherings, and rulers' courts, involving both Muslim and non-Muslim scholars. This sets the stage for a detailed study of the principles and methods of dialectical debate in the Islamic tradition.

Key Terms
الجدل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what were the two purposes of jadal as derived from the Quran?
A) To refute and to convince
B) To entertain and to teach
C) To divide and to rule
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
Jadal is a Quranically-rooted method for seeking truth through disciplined debate, used by Muslim scholars across all Islamic sciences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Read a passage from a usul al-fiqh work (e.g., al-Amidi's al-Ihkam) where two opinions are presented; identify how the author uses jadal techniques to present evidence and counter-evidence.
?
Write a short paragraph explaining how the Quranic use of jadal differs from common negative perceptions of debate as quarreling or sophistry.

Dialectic -- Jadal
intermediate
8 min
Jadal: Universal yet Distinctly Human
Author discusses the abundance of human jadal with Quranic evidence and commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why jadal is both a universal phenomenon and specifically human, using evidence from the Quran and Ibn Ashur's commentary.

Core Idea
Jadal is universal but human jadal is distinctive because it springs from speech (nutq), the differentia of humanity.

The author starts by affirming that jadal is not unique to humans—it appears throughout creation. Yet humans are singled out as the most argumentative. How can this be? The key lies in the human capacity for nutq (speech/rationality), which makes jadal a defining human activity. Ibn Ashur’s interpretation of the Quranic verse resolves the tension: the verse emphasizes the intensity of human jadal, not a comparison with non-human creatures that cannot argue.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the universal claim
The author states that jadal is a universal phenomenon (ظاهرة كونية) not limited to humans. Identify the sentence in the Arabic that makes this claim.
It's the second sentence: 'مع أن الجدل - كما قلنا - ظاهرة كونية لا يتميز بها الإنسان وحده'
2
Identify the human-specific element
The author explains that humans are the most capable and practiced in jadal. Later, Ibn Ashur specifies that jadal is a branch of nutq, which is the differentia of humanity. Find where nutq is mentioned.
Ibn Ashur says: 'الجدل خاص بالإنسان لأنه من شعب النطق الذي هو فصل حقيقة الإنسانية'
3
Analyze Ibn Ashur's linguistic insight
Ibn Ashur argues that the comparative form 'akthar' (أكثر) is actually hyperbolic (maslub al-mufadala). Why does he say that? Because non-human earthly creatures cannot engage in jadal at all, so a true comparison is impossible. The form is used for emphasis, not comparison.
4
Distinguish human jadal from angelic and satanic jadal
Ibn Ashur notes that angels do engage in jadal but it is praiseworthy, while devils are even more argumentative than humans. However, the verse context excludes these. Identify the Quranic example of angelic jadal given in the passage.
It's the angels' question in Surah Al-Baqarah: 'أَتَجْعَلُ فِيهَا مَن يُفْسِدُ فِيهَا'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المطلب الثاني : كثرة جدل الإنسان
مع أن الجدل - كما قلنا - ظاهرة كونية لا يتميز بها الإنسان وحده، إلا أنه أكثر المخلوقات قدرة عليها وأشدها تمرنًا عليها واستعمالا لها . حتى إن الله عز وجل وصف الإنسان بأنه أكثر مخلوقاته جدلا، فقال تعالى : وَلَقَدْ صَرَّفْنَا فِي هَذَا الْقُرْءَانِ لِلنَّاسِ مِن كُلِّ مَثَلِ وَكَانَ الْإِنسَنُ أَكْثَرَ شَيْءٍ جَدَلًا.
فجدل الإنسان لا يقف عند حد معين، بل إنه يمتد ليشمل كل موقع فيه الإنسان كائنا ما كان هذا الموقع، إذ يجد نفسه دائمًا في حاجة إلى ممارسة الجدل لكي يحقق ذاته في هذا الموقع الذي يوجد فيه، بالتأمل فيما يلزمه عمله، ثم بالتصريح برأيه والكشف عن نتيجة تأمله وإدارة الجدل حولها مع غيره الذي قد يكون مخالفًا له فيما انتهى إليه.
ويرى الشيخ محمد الطاهر بن عاشور رحمه الله أن اسم التفضيل (أكثر) في هذه الآية مسلوب المفاضلة . . . وإنما أتى بصيغته لقصد المبالغة في شدة جدل الإنسان وجنوحه إلى المماراة والنزاع حتى فيما ترك الجدال في شأنه أحسن، بحيث إن شدة الوصف فيه تشبه تفوقه في الوصف على كل من يعرض أنه موصوف به .
ف ( أكثر ) لم يرد في مقام المقارنة بين الإنسان وغيره، وإنما ورد في مقام الحديث عن كثرة جدل الإنسان ذاته، ويبرر رأيه هذا بقوله : وإنما ألجئنا إلى هذا التأويل في اسم التفضيل لظهور أن غير الإنسان من أنواع ما على الأرض لا يتصور منه الجدل، فالجدل خاص بالإنسان لأنه من شعب النطق الذي هو فصل حقيقة الإنسانية، أما الملائكة فجدلهم محمود مثل قوله : قَالُوا أَتَجْعَلُ فِيهَا مَن يُفْسِدُ فِيهَا وَيَسْفِكُ الدِّمَاءَ إلى قوله : وَنُقَدِّسُ لَكَ ، وأما الشياطين فهم أكثر جدلاً من الإنسان، ولكن لما نبا المقام عن إرادتهم كانوا غير مرادين بالتفضيل عليهم في الجدل.
وسواء كان ما ذهب إليه الإمام تأويلا راجحًا أو مرجوحا، فإن المراد هنا، كما ذهب هو نفسه مطلق الجدل، وخاصة ما كان منه بباطل، أي أن كل إنسان في طبعه الحرص على إقناع المخالف بأحقية معتقده أو عمله.
فجدل الإنسان كثير لا يدخل تحت حصر، إن في الكم أو في الكيف، فالكثرة في الكم يمثلها عرض الحجة الواحدة بعدد وفير من أساليب القول، والإنسان يفعل ذلك طمعًا بأن أسلوبًا كلاميًا منها قد يؤثر فيمن يجادله . . والكثرة في الكيف يمثلها كثرة الأنواع والصور الفكرية التي يجادل الإنسان فيها أو يستخدمها في جداله، ومن ذلك أن يجادل الإنسان فيما له به حجة، وفيما ليس له به حجة أو شبه حجة، أو رائحة دليل، وقد يتمسك بما هو ظاهر الفساد والبطلان، لأن له هوى في ذلك، ويحاول بكل وسيلة جدلية أن يقلب الباطل حقا والحق باطلا، وأن يتظاهر بأن الحق في جانبه مع أنه لا دليل له إلا الكذب في القول.
قال أحد المفسرين في التعليق على قوله تعالى: ﴿وَكَانَ الْإِنسَنُ أَكْثَرَ شَيْءٍ جَدَلًا : (يعني : أن الأشياء التي يتأتى منها الجدل إن فصلتها واحدا بعد واحد، فإن الإنسان أكثرها خصومة، فقوله ( أكثر شيء كقوله (أول مرة) في الأنعام ).
وكثرة جدل الإنسان لسعة مضطربه فيما بين أوج الملكية إلى حضيض البهيمية فليس له في جانبي التصاعد والتسافل مقام معلوم.
The Second Demand: The Abundance of Human Jadal
Even though jadal - as we said - is a universal phenomenon not exclusive to humans, yet he is the most capable of creatures regarding it and the most practiced and employing of it. So much so that Allah Almighty described the human as the most argumentative of His creatures, saying: 'And We have certainly diversified in this Qur'an for the people every kind of example, but man has been, of all things, most argumentative.'
For human jadal does not stop at a specific limit, but rather it extends to include every position in which a human is, whatever that position may be, as he always finds himself in need of practicing jadal in order to actualize himself in that position he is in, by contemplating what he must do, then by expressing his opinion and revealing the result of his contemplation and managing jadal about it with others who may disagree with him regarding what he concluded.
And Sheikh Muhammad al-Tahir ibn Ashur, may Allah have mercy on him, holds that the comparative noun (akthar) in this verse is stripped of comparison... Rather, it is brought in its form for the purpose of hyperbole in the intensity of human jadal and his inclination to disputation and contention, even regarding matters where refraining from jadal would be better, such that the intensity of the description resembles his surpassing in description over anyone it is claimed he is described with.
Thus, (akthar) was not intended in the context of comparison between humans and others, but rather it came in the context of talking about the abundance of human jadal itself. He justifies this opinion by saying: We were forced to this interpretation of the comparative noun because it is evident that other than humans from the types of things on earth are not conceived to engage in jadal, for jadal is specific to humans because it is one of the branches of speech, which is the differentia of humanity. As for angels, their jadal is praiseworthy, such as His saying: 'They said, Will You place upon it one who causes corruption therein and sheds blood?' until His saying: 'while we exalt You with praise.' And as for devils, they are more argumentative than humans, but since the context was not intended for them, they were not meant by the preference in jadal.
Whether the Imam's interpretation is preponderant or weak, the intended meaning here, as he himself held, is absolute jadal, especially that which is with falsehood, meaning that every human by nature is keen on convincing the opponent of the rightness of his belief or action.
Thus, human jadal is abundant and cannot be confined, whether in quantity or in quality. The abundance in quantity is represented by presenting a single argument through numerous styles of speech, and a human does that hoping that a verbal style from among them may affect the one he is arguing with... And the abundance in quality is represented by the abundance of intellectual types and forms in which a human argues or which he uses in his argument. From that is that a human argues regarding that for which he has proof, and regarding that for which he has no proof, or a semblance of proof, or a whiff of evidence, and he may cling to what is manifestly corrupt and false because he has passion for that, and he tries by every dialectical means to turn falsehood into truth and truth into falsehood, and to pretend that truth is on his side while he has no proof except lying in speech.
One of the commentators said in commenting on His statement: 'and man has been, of all things, most argumentative': (Meaning: the things from which jadal can arise, if you analyze them one by one, then man is the most quarrelsome among them. So His saying 'most thing' is like His saying 'the first time' in Surat al-An'am).
And the abundance of human jadal is due to the vastness of his fluctuation between the peak of angelic nature and the nadir of bestiality; he has no fixed station in the directions of ascent and descent.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage discusses the abundance of human jadal (dialectic/argumentation). The author begins by acknowledging that jadal is a universal phenomenon not limited to humans, but humans are the most capable and practiced in it. He cites the Quranic verse (Surah al-Kahf: 54) where Allah describes man as the most argumentative of things. The author then explains that human jadal extends to every situation, as humans constantly need to argue to assert themselves. He then presents the interpretation of Sheikh Muhammad al-Tahir ibn Ashur, who argues that the comparative form 'akthar' (most) in the verse is not actually comparative but hyperbolic, meaning that man is extremely argumentative, not that he is more argumentative than others. Ibn Ashur justifies this by noting that non-human entities on earth cannot engage in jadal because jadal requires speech, which is specific to humans. He distinguishes human jadal from that of angels (praiseworthy) and devils (more argumentative but not intended in the verse). The author then concludes that the verse refers to absolute jadal, especially false argumentation, and that every human naturally seeks to convince others of their beliefs. Finally, the author discusses the quantitative and qualitative abundance of human jadal: quantitatively, humans present many styles of argument for a single point; qualitatively, they argue about things with or without proof, even using falsehood and sophistry. The passage ends with a quote from another commentator explaining the verse and noting the vast range of human jadal due to man's intermediate nature between angels and animals.

Key Terms
الجدل
اسم التفضيل
المفاضلة
النطق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Ashur's interpretation in the passage, why is the word 'akthar' (most) in the verse not actually comparative?
A) Because humans are not the most argumentative creatures; devils are.
B) Because non-human earthly creatures cannot engage in jadal, so comparison is impossible.
C) Because the verse was abrogated.
D) Because 'akthar' is a homonym with a different meaning.

Key Takeaway
Jadal is a human-specific phenomenon rooted in speech (nutq), and the Quranic description of man as 'most argumentative' is hyperbolic emphasis, not a literal comparison.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In Surah Al-Baqarah (2:30), the angels question Allah about creating humans: 'Will You place upon it one who causes corruption therein?' Identify how this angelic jadal differs from human jadal according to Ibn Ashur's classification (praiseworthy vs. disputatious).
?
Find another Quranic verse where a comparative form (ism tafdil) is used hyperbolically. Explain why the literal comparative reading would be problematic, similar to Ibn Ashur's argument.

Dialectic -- Jadal
beginner
6 min
Quantitative and Qualitative Abundance of Human Jadal
Author discusses the abundance of human jadal with Quranic evidence and commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between quantitative and qualitative abundance of human jadal and provide examples of each from Islamic scholarly practice.

Core Idea
Human jadal is abundant in quantity (multiple styles for one argument) and quality (varied topics, from truth to falsehood).

The author further elaborates on the abundance of human jadal by dividing it into two dimensions: quantitative and qualitative. Quantitatively, a single point can be argued using countless rhetorical styles. Qualitatively, humans argue about a vast range of subjects, sometimes even defending falsehood out of desire. This duality reflects the human condition, fluctuating between angelic and bestial tendencies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two dimensions of abundance
The author explicitly mentions 'الكثرة في الكم' (abundance in quantity) and 'الكثرة في الكيف' (abundance in quality). Find these phrases in the Arabic and note what they refer to.
They appear after the discussion of Ibn Ashur's interpretation.
2
Analyze quantitative abundance
The author says that a single argument (الحجة الواحدة) is presented through many verbal styles. Why does a person do this? To increase the chance of influencing the opponent. In fiqh, a jurist might present multiple qiyas (analogies) to support a ruling.
3
Analyze qualitative abundance
Qualitative abundance refers to the many types of intellectual forms used in argumentation. The author lists: arguing with proof, without proof, with semblance of proof, or even with manifest falsehood. This shows the moral dimension of jadal.
The author mentions that a person may cling to falsehood due to desire (هوى).
4
Connect to human nature
The passage ends by linking the vastness of human jadal to man's intermediate station between angels and animals. Humans can ascend to angelic debate or descend to bestial quarreling. This explains the wide spectrum of argumentation quality.
The phrase 'بين أوج الملكية إلى حضيض البهيمية' captures this.

Source Text

المطلب الثاني : كثرة جدل الإنسان
مع أن الجدل - كما قلنا - ظاهرة كونية لا يتميز بها الإنسان وحده، إلا أنه أكثر المخلوقات قدرة عليها وأشدها تمرنًا عليها واستعمالا لها . حتى إن الله عز وجل وصف الإنسان بأنه أكثر مخلوقاته جدلا، فقال تعالى : وَلَقَدْ صَرَّفْنَا فِي هَذَا الْقُرْءَانِ لِلنَّاسِ مِن كُلِّ مَثَلِ وَكَانَ الْإِنسَنُ أَكْثَرَ شَيْءٍ جَدَلًا.
فجدل الإنسان لا يقف عند حد معين، بل إنه يمتد ليشمل كل موقع فيه الإنسان كائنا ما كان هذا الموقع، إذ يجد نفسه دائمًا في حاجة إلى ممارسة الجدل لكي يحقق ذاته في هذا الموقع الذي يوجد فيه، بالتأمل فيما يلزمه عمله، ثم بالتصريح برأيه والكشف عن نتيجة تأمله وإدارة الجدل حولها مع غيره الذي قد يكون مخالفًا له فيما انتهى إليه.
ويرى الشيخ محمد الطاهر بن عاشور رحمه الله أن اسم التفضيل (أكثر) في هذه الآية مسلوب المفاضلة . . . وإنما أتى بصيغته لقصد المبالغة في شدة جدل الإنسان وجنوحه إلى المماراة والنزاع حتى فيما ترك الجدال في شأنه أحسن، بحيث إن شدة الوصف فيه تشبه تفوقه في الوصف على كل من يعرض أنه موصوف به .
ف ( أكثر ) لم يرد في مقام المقارنة بين الإنسان وغيره، وإنما ورد في مقام الحديث عن كثرة جدل الإنسان ذاته، ويبرر رأيه هذا بقوله : وإنما ألجئنا إلى هذا التأويل في اسم التفضيل لظهور أن غير الإنسان من أنواع ما على الأرض لا يتصور منه الجدل، فالجدل خاص بالإنسان لأنه من شعب النطق الذي هو فصل حقيقة الإنسانية، أما الملائكة فجدلهم محمود مثل قوله : قَالُوا أَتَجْعَلُ فِيهَا مَن يُفْسِدُ فِيهَا وَيَسْفِكُ الدِّمَاءَ إلى قوله : وَنُقَدِّسُ لَكَ ، وأما الشياطين فهم أكثر جدلاً من الإنسان، ولكن لما نبا المقام عن إرادتهم كانوا غير مرادين بالتفضيل عليهم في الجدل.
وسواء كان ما ذهب إليه الإمام تأويلا راجحًا أو مرجوحا، فإن المراد هنا، كما ذهب هو نفسه مطلق الجدل، وخاصة ما كان منه بباطل، أي أن كل إنسان في طبعه الحرص على إقناع المخالف بأحقية معتقده أو عمله.
فجدل الإنسان كثير لا يدخل تحت حصر، إن في الكم أو في الكيف، فالكثرة في الكم يمثلها عرض الحجة الواحدة بعدد وفير من أساليب القول، والإنسان يفعل ذلك طمعًا بأن أسلوبًا كلاميًا منها قد يؤثر فيمن يجادله . . والكثرة في الكيف يمثلها كثرة الأنواع والصور الفكرية التي يجادل الإنسان فيها أو يستخدمها في جداله، ومن ذلك أن يجادل الإنسان فيما له به حجة، وفيما ليس له به حجة أو شبه حجة، أو رائحة دليل، وقد يتمسك بما هو ظاهر الفساد والبطلان، لأن له هوى في ذلك، ويحاول بكل وسيلة جدلية أن يقلب الباطل حقا والحق باطلا، وأن يتظاهر بأن الحق في جانبه مع أنه لا دليل له إلا الكذب في القول.
قال أحد المفسرين في التعليق على قوله تعالى: ﴿وَكَانَ الْإِنسَنُ أَكْثَرَ شَيْءٍ جَدَلًا : (يعني : أن الأشياء التي يتأتى منها الجدل إن فصلتها واحدا بعد واحد، فإن الإنسان أكثرها خصومة، فقوله ( أكثر شيء كقوله (أول مرة) في الأنعام ).
وكثرة جدل الإنسان لسعة مضطربه فيما بين أوج الملكية إلى حضيض البهيمية فليس له في جانبي التصاعد والتسافل مقام معلوم.
The Second Demand: The Abundance of Human Jadal
Even though jadal - as we said - is a universal phenomenon not exclusive to humans, yet he is the most capable of creatures regarding it and the most practiced and employing of it. So much so that Allah Almighty described the human as the most argumentative of His creatures, saying: 'And We have certainly diversified in this Qur'an for the people every kind of example, but man has been, of all things, most argumentative.'
For human jadal does not stop at a specific limit, but rather it extends to include every position in which a human is, whatever that position may be, as he always finds himself in need of practicing jadal in order to actualize himself in that position he is in, by contemplating what he must do, then by expressing his opinion and revealing the result of his contemplation and managing jadal about it with others who may disagree with him regarding what he concluded.
And Sheikh Muhammad al-Tahir ibn Ashur, may Allah have mercy on him, holds that the comparative noun (akthar) in this verse is stripped of comparison... Rather, it is brought in its form for the purpose of hyperbole in the intensity of human jadal and his inclination to disputation and contention, even regarding matters where refraining from jadal would be better, such that the intensity of the description resembles his surpassing in description over anyone it is claimed he is described with.
Thus, (akthar) was not intended in the context of comparison between humans and others, but rather it came in the context of talking about the abundance of human jadal itself. He justifies this opinion by saying: We were forced to this interpretation of the comparative noun because it is evident that other than humans from the types of things on earth are not conceived to engage in jadal, for jadal is specific to humans because it is one of the branches of speech, which is the differentia of humanity. As for angels, their jadal is praiseworthy, such as His saying: 'They said, Will You place upon it one who causes corruption therein and sheds blood?' until His saying: 'while we exalt You with praise.' And as for devils, they are more argumentative than humans, but since the context was not intended for them, they were not meant by the preference in jadal.
Whether the Imam's interpretation is preponderant or weak, the intended meaning here, as he himself held, is absolute jadal, especially that which is with falsehood, meaning that every human by nature is keen on convincing the opponent of the rightness of his belief or action.
Thus, human jadal is abundant and cannot be confined, whether in quantity or in quality. The abundance in quantity is represented by presenting a single argument through numerous styles of speech, and a human does that hoping that a verbal style from among them may affect the one he is arguing with... And the abundance in quality is represented by the abundance of intellectual types and forms in which a human argues or which he uses in his argument. From that is that a human argues regarding that for which he has proof, and regarding that for which he has no proof, or a semblance of proof, or a whiff of evidence, and he may cling to what is manifestly corrupt and false because he has passion for that, and he tries by every dialectical means to turn falsehood into truth and truth into falsehood, and to pretend that truth is on his side while he has no proof except lying in speech.
One of the commentators said in commenting on His statement: 'and man has been, of all things, most argumentative': (Meaning: the things from which jadal can arise, if you analyze them one by one, then man is the most quarrelsome among them. So His saying 'most thing' is like His saying 'the first time' in Surat al-An'am).
And the abundance of human jadal is due to the vastness of his fluctuation between the peak of angelic nature and the nadir of bestiality; he has no fixed station in the directions of ascent and descent.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage discusses the abundance of human jadal (dialectic/argumentation). The author begins by acknowledging that jadal is a universal phenomenon not limited to humans, but humans are the most capable and practiced in it. He cites the Quranic verse (Surah al-Kahf: 54) where Allah describes man as the most argumentative of things. The author then explains that human jadal extends to every situation, as humans constantly need to argue to assert themselves. He then presents the interpretation of Sheikh Muhammad al-Tahir ibn Ashur, who argues that the comparative form 'akthar' (most) in the verse is not actually comparative but hyperbolic, meaning that man is extremely argumentative, not that he is more argumentative than others. Ibn Ashur justifies this by noting that non-human entities on earth cannot engage in jadal because jadal requires speech, which is specific to humans. He distinguishes human jadal from that of angels (praiseworthy) and devils (more argumentative but not intended in the verse). The author then concludes that the verse refers to absolute jadal, especially false argumentation, and that every human naturally seeks to convince others of their beliefs. Finally, the author discusses the quantitative and qualitative abundance of human jadal: quantitatively, humans present many styles of argument for a single point; qualitatively, they argue about things with or without proof, even using falsehood and sophistry. The passage ends with a quote from another commentator explaining the verse and noting the vast range of human jadal due to man's intermediate nature between angels and animals.

Key Terms
الكم
الكيف
الهوى
الحجة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does 'abundance in quality' of human jadal refer to?
A) The number of people engaged in jadal.
B) The variety of intellectual types and forms of argumentation.
C) The loudness of voices during debate.
D) The length of time spent arguing.

Key Takeaway
Human jadal is abundant in both the variety of argumentative styles (quantity) and the range of epistemic and moral qualities (quality), reflecting man's intermediate nature between angelic and bestial.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In a fiqh debate on the permissibility of cryptocurrency, a scholar presents three different qiyas to argue it is halal. Identify whether this is an example of quantitative or qualitative abundance and explain why.
?
The author describes someone who clings to manifest falsehood due to passion (هوى). Give a historical example from Islamic sectarian debates (e.g., between Khawarij and early Muslims) where this occurred, and explain how it fits the qualitative abundance category.

The Human Capacity for Disputation and the Role of Desire
Author discusses human capacity for disputation and the role of desire.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the psychological factors that lead people to argue for falsehood instead of truth, as described in classical Islamic texts.

Core Idea
Disputation is a human tool; desire (hawa) turns it from a path to truth into a weapon for falsehood.

The passage begins by noting that Allah describes man as the most disputatious of creatures. This capacity exists from the beginning and is used for both truth and falsehood. However, most people use it for falsehood because of the dominance of personal desires. The author explains that desire blinds one's insight, so the individual sees only what his whims dictate, even to his own destruction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim about human disputation
Find the author's description of man's ability to argue. What evidence from Quran is given?
2
Extract the reasons for arguing for falsehood
List the psychological factors the author mentions that lead people to argue for falsehood.
Look for terms like 'hawa', 'deception', 'evasion'.
3
Contrast with argumentation for truth
Note when people argue for truth (prophets, preachers). What motivates them?
4
Understand the concept of 'hawa'
How does desire affect argumentation according to the passage?
Hawa dominates the soul and covers insight.
5
Apply to a real-world scenario
Think of a modern debate where one side seems driven by desire. How does the passage help analyze it?
Avoid actual examples; focus on the framework.

المطلب الثالث : جدل الإنسان بين الحق والباطل
إن وصف الله عز وجل للإنسان بأنه أكثر شيء جدلا، دليل على مبلغ قدرته على الحيلة الفكرية التي تمكنه من أن يجادل بالحق أو بالباطل، ويكر ويفر ويراوغ في المجادلة.
وقد توفرت هذه المقدرة في الإنسان منذ بدء وجوده على هذه الأرض، حيث عرف منذ نشأته الأولى كيف يداور ويحاور في القول ومرن على مجادلة الغير. كسبيل ينفذ من خلاله إلى تحقيق مصالحه وإقناع الآخرين بتمكينه من تلك المصالح، عن طريق التبادل أو التنازل، ولم يكن يتورع عن استخدام هذه الوسيلة حتى في سلب حقوق الآخرين وهضمها، فضلا عن استخدامه لها في الحصول على حقوقه المشروعة.
ويشهد التاريخ الإنساني، أن الإنسان وإن كان قد استعمل الجدل في الحق في بعض الأحيان، كما كان حال الرسل والأنبياء والدعاة، فقد استعمله في الباطل أكثر الأحيان، إذ شهدت أغلب فترات التاريخ محاولة الإنسان إقرار الباطل وغمط الحق باعتماد الحيل المتنوعة، القائمة على الخداع والختل والمراوغة والتزيين بالقول في مكر ودهاء.. ويرجع سبب انتصار الإنسان للباطل على حساب الحق في أكثر الأحيان إلى سيطرة نوازع الهوى على نفسه وتغطيتها على منافذ رؤيته وبصيرته فيصبح لا يرى إلا ما يمليه عليه هواه حتى وإن كان فيه هلاكه ودمار حياته.
لكن الغريب في سلوك الإنسان، أنه حين تدفعه أهواؤه وشهواته الجانحة إلى تجاوز دائرة الحق والعدل والخير والفضيلة، ويظل ذلك حريصًا على أن يظهر أمام الناس بمظهر الكمال تتولد عنده الرغبة الشديدة بأن يثبت سلامة تصرفه وصحة منهجه في الحياة، فيلجأ إلى خطة التزيين والتبرير بالباطل، فإذا وجد مخالفة أو معارضة لجأ إلى خطة الجدال، وفي الجدال يصنع ما يصنع المقاتل راغبًا بالانتصار على خصمه لا حريصًا على الوصول إلى الحق بالمناظرة الشريفة العفيفة.
ومع أن الإنسان في العادة يعلم بما يخفيه في نفسه من حرص على إقرار الباطل والتنكر للحق، يظل مع ذلك يجادل في سبيل الباطل، دفعا للتكاليف الثقيلة عن نفسه واتباعًا للهوى الذي فيه إشباع لملذاته وشهواته وقد كشف الله عز وجل عن هذه الطبيعة في نفس الإنسان، فقال يصف منكري البعث الذين يجادلون فيه جحودا وإنكارا، رغبة في الاستغراق في متع الحياة الدنيا : ﴿بَل يُرِيدُ الإِنسَنُ لِيَفْجُرَ أَمَامَهُ يَسْتَلُ أَيَّانَ يَوْمُ الْقِيَامَةِ﴾، فهو ينكر اليوم الآخر، وينكر البعث والنشور لا اقتناعا بأن ذلك لن يكون، وإنما لكي يقنع نفسه بأن ما يخوض فيه من فسوق وعصيان وانسياق وراء الأهواء والشهوات حق ينبغي اتباعه وعدم الانحراف عنه، مع أنه يدرك في قرارة نفسه أنه باطل لا يجوز له الخوض فيه، وقال الله تعالى: ﴿وَمِنَ النَّاسِ مَن يُجَدِلُ فِي اللَّهِ بِغَيْرِ عِلْمٍ وَيَتَّبِعُ كُلَّ شَيْطَانٍ مريد﴾، وقال : ﴿وَمِنَ النَّاسِ مَن يُجَدِلُ فِي اللهِ بِغَيْرِ عِلْمٍ وَلَا هُدًى وَلَا كِتَابٍ مُنِيرٍ. لِيُضِلَّ عَن سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ لَهُ فِي الدُّنْيَا خِزْيٌ وَنُذِيقَهُ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ عَذَابَ الحريق﴾.
وقد عرف تاريخ الدعوة النبوية معاناة الرسل مع هذا النوع من الناس، وهم أكثر الخلق، إذ قابلهم هؤلاء بالمنازعة والجدل العنيف في الكثير من الأحيان، المصحوب بالأذى حين تعجزهم الحيل الفكرية والقولية. قال تعالى: ﴿وَمَا نُرْسِلُ الْمُرْسَلِينَ إِلَّا مُبَشِّرِينَ وَمُنذِرِينَ وَيُجَادِلُ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا بِالْبَاطِلِ لِيُدْحِضُوا بِهِ الْحَقَّ وَاتَّخَذُوا آيَاتِي وَمَا أُنذِرُوا هُزُوًا﴾. وقال عز وجل، ﴿مَا يُجَادِلُ فِي آيَاتِ اللهِ إِلَّا الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا فَلَا يَغْرُرُكَ تَقَلُّبُهُمْ فِي الْبِلَادِ كَذَّبَتْ قَبْلَهُمْ قَوْمُ نُوحٍ وَالْأَحْزَابُ مِنْ بَعْدِهِمْ وَهَمَّتْ كُلُّ أُمَّةٍ بِرَسُولِهِمْ﴾
The third demand: Man's disputation between truth and falsehood. Indeed, Allah's description of man as the most disputatious of things is evidence of the extent of his ability for intellectual trickery that enables him to argue with truth or falsehood, and to attack, retreat, and maneuver in argument. This ability has been available in man since the beginning of his existence on this earth, for he knew from his earliest formation how to parley and converse in speech and trained himself to argue with others. As a means through which he achieves his interests and persuades others to enable him to obtain those interests, through exchange or concession, and he did not refrain from using this means even to usurp and swallow the rights of others, let alone using it to obtain his legitimate rights. Human history bears witness that although man used argumentation for truth at times, as was the case of messengers, prophets, and preachers, he used it for falsehood most of the time, as most periods of history witnessed man's attempt to establish falsehood and suppress truth by adopting various tricks based on deception, fraud, evasion, and embellishment of speech with cunning and guile. The reason for man's victory of falsehood at the expense of truth in most cases is due to the domination of the inclinations of desire over his soul and their covering the outlets of his vision and insight, so that he sees only what his desire dictates even if it contains his destruction and ruin of his life. But strange in man's behavior is that when his uncontrolled desires and lusts push him to exceed the circle of truth, justice, goodness, and virtue, and he remains careful to appear before people in the guise of perfection, there arises in him an intense desire to prove the soundness of his conduct and the correctness of his method in life, so he resorts to the plan of embellishment and justification with falsehood, and if he encounters opposition or objection, he resorts to the plan of argumentation, and in argumentation he acts like a fighter desiring victory over his opponent, not careful to reach the truth through honorable and chaste debate. And although man usually knows what he hides in himself of eagerness to establish falsehood and deny truth, he still argues in the cause of falsehood, to repel heavy burdens from himself and follow desire which contains gratification of his pleasures and lusts. Allah has revealed this nature in man's soul, saying describing the deniers of resurrection who argue about it in denial and rejection, desiring to immerse themselves in the pleasures of worldly life: 'But man desires to persist in his sinful ways, asking, When is the Day of Resurrection?' So he denies the Last Day, and denies resurrection and gathering, not out of conviction that it will not happen, but to convince himself that what he indulges in of transgression, disobedience, and following desires and lusts is truth that should be followed and not deviated from, while he knows in the depths of his soul that it is falsehood that he should not indulge in. And Allah said: 'And among the people is he who disputes about Allah without knowledge and follows every rebellious devil.' And He said: 'And among the people is he who disputes about Allah without knowledge, without guidance, and without an enlightening book, to lead others astray from the way of Allah. For him in this world is disgrace, and on the Day of Resurrection We will make him taste the punishment of the burning fire.' The history of the prophetic call has known the suffering of the messengers with this type of people, who are the majority of creation, for these people confronted them with contention and violent argument many times, accompanied by harm when intellectual and verbal tricks fail them. Allah said: 'And We send the messengers only as bearers of good news and as warners. But those who disbelieve argue with falsehood to rebut the truth thereby, and they take My signs and that of which they are warned in mockery.' And He said: 'None dispute concerning the signs of Allah except those who disbelieve, so let not their striding about in the land delude you. The people of Noah denied before them, and the parties after them, and every nation plotted against their messenger.'
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is an exposition on the nature of human disputation (jadal), focusing on man's propensity to argue for falsehood. The author begins by stating that Allah's description of man as 'most disputatious' indicates his capacity for intellectual trickery, which he can use for either truth or falsehood. This ability has been present since the beginning of human existence. The author then notes that while man has used argumentation for truth (as prophets and preachers did), he more often uses it for falsehood, employing deception, evasion, and embellishment. The reason for this is the dominance of personal desires (hawa) over his soul, blinding him so that he only follows his whims even to his own destruction. Strangely, when desires push him beyond the bounds of truth, he still wants to appear perfect, so he justifies his actions with falsehood and, when opposed, resorts to argumentation like a fighter seeking victory, not truth. Even though he knows inwardly that he is defending falsehood, he continues to argue out of desire and to avoid burdens. The author then supports this with Quranic verses: verses about the deniers of resurrection who argue out of desire to continue sinning, and verses condemning those who dispute about Allah without knowledge, following devils, to mislead others. Finally, the author references the history of prophets who suffered from such people who argued violently and harmed them when intellectual tricks failed, citing Quranic verses that describe the disbelievers arguing with falsehood to rebut the truth and taking Allah's signs in mockery.

Key Terms
الجدل
الحق
الباطل
الهوى

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason people often argue for falsehood instead of truth?
A) They are convinced that falsehood is truth.
B) The domination of their desires (hawa) over their soul.
C) They lack the intellectual ability to argue for truth.
D) They want to impress others with their debating skills.

Key Takeaway
Human disputation is driven by desire; only by purifying intentions can one argue for truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify a contemporary debate (e.g., about a fiqh ruling) where one party seems to argue out of desire rather than truth. List three signs from the passage (e.g., use of deception, evasion, desire for victory) that indicate this.
?

Quranic Condemnation of Disputation for Falsehood
Author cites Quranic verses condemning disputation for falsehood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze Quranic verses about disputation and explain their logical and moral implications.

Core Idea
The Quran condemns arguing without knowledge and for the purpose of misleading others.

The author supports his analysis with several Quranic verses. These verses describe those who dispute about Allah without knowledge, follow rebellious devils, and seek to lead others astray. The passage also cites the history of prophets who faced such disputation from disbelievers who argued with falsehood to rebut the truth.

Guided Path
1
List the Quranic verses cited
Identify all the verses referenced in the passage and note their themes.
Verses include: 'Bal yurid al-insanu...', 'Wa min al-nasi man yujadilu...', etc.
2
Identify common elements
What do these verses say about the motives and methods of the disputants?
Look for words like 'bila ilm', 'yunadi', 'yujadilu bil-batil'.
3
Analyze the verse about signs of Allah
What does 'None dispute concerning the signs of Allah except those who disbelieve' imply?
This verse from Surah Ghafir is key.
4
Connect to prophetic experience
How did the prophets suffer from these disputants according to the passage and verses?
The passage mentions harm when intellectual tricks fail.

المطلب الثالث : جدل الإنسان بين الحق والباطل
إن وصف الله عز وجل للإنسان بأنه أكثر شيء جدلا، دليل على مبلغ قدرته على الحيلة الفكرية التي تمكنه من أن يجادل بالحق أو بالباطل، ويكر ويفر ويراوغ في المجادلة.
وقد توفرت هذه المقدرة في الإنسان منذ بدء وجوده على هذه الأرض، حيث عرف منذ نشأته الأولى كيف يداور ويحاور في القول ومرن على مجادلة الغير. كسبيل ينفذ من خلاله إلى تحقيق مصالحه وإقناع الآخرين بتمكينه من تلك المصالح، عن طريق التبادل أو التنازل، ولم يكن يتورع عن استخدام هذه الوسيلة حتى في سلب حقوق الآخرين وهضمها، فضلا عن استخدامه لها في الحصول على حقوقه المشروعة.
ويشهد التاريخ الإنساني، أن الإنسان وإن كان قد استعمل الجدل في الحق في بعض الأحيان، كما كان حال الرسل والأنبياء والدعاة، فقد استعمله في الباطل أكثر الأحيان، إذ شهدت أغلب فترات التاريخ محاولة الإنسان إقرار الباطل وغمط الحق باعتماد الحيل المتنوعة، القائمة على الخداع والختل والمراوغة والتزيين بالقول في مكر ودهاء.. ويرجع سبب انتصار الإنسان للباطل على حساب الحق في أكثر الأحيان إلى سيطرة نوازع الهوى على نفسه وتغطيتها على منافذ رؤيته وبصيرته فيصبح لا يرى إلا ما يمليه عليه هواه حتى وإن كان فيه هلاكه ودمار حياته.
لكن الغريب في سلوك الإنسان، أنه حين تدفعه أهواؤه وشهواته الجانحة إلى تجاوز دائرة الحق والعدل والخير والفضيلة، ويظل ذلك حريصًا على أن يظهر أمام الناس بمظهر الكمال تتولد عنده الرغبة الشديدة بأن يثبت سلامة تصرفه وصحة منهجه في الحياة، فيلجأ إلى خطة التزيين والتبرير بالباطل، فإذا وجد مخالفة أو معارضة لجأ إلى خطة الجدال، وفي الجدال يصنع ما يصنع المقاتل راغبًا بالانتصار على خصمه لا حريصًا على الوصول إلى الحق بالمناظرة الشريفة العفيفة.
ومع أن الإنسان في العادة يعلم بما يخفيه في نفسه من حرص على إقرار الباطل والتنكر للحق، يظل مع ذلك يجادل في سبيل الباطل، دفعا للتكاليف الثقيلة عن نفسه واتباعًا للهوى الذي فيه إشباع لملذاته وشهواته وقد كشف الله عز وجل عن هذه الطبيعة في نفس الإنسان، فقال يصف منكري البعث الذين يجادلون فيه جحودا وإنكارا، رغبة في الاستغراق في متع الحياة الدنيا : ﴿بَل يُرِيدُ الإِنسَنُ لِيَفْجُرَ أَمَامَهُ يَسْتَلُ أَيَّانَ يَوْمُ الْقِيَامَةِ﴾، فهو ينكر اليوم الآخر، وينكر البعث والنشور لا اقتناعا بأن ذلك لن يكون، وإنما لكي يقنع نفسه بأن ما يخوض فيه من فسوق وعصيان وانسياق وراء الأهواء والشهوات حق ينبغي اتباعه وعدم الانحراف عنه، مع أنه يدرك في قرارة نفسه أنه باطل لا يجوز له الخوض فيه، وقال الله تعالى: ﴿وَمِنَ النَّاسِ مَن يُجَدِلُ فِي اللَّهِ بِغَيْرِ عِلْمٍ وَيَتَّبِعُ كُلَّ شَيْطَانٍ مريد﴾، وقال : ﴿وَمِنَ النَّاسِ مَن يُجَدِلُ فِي اللهِ بِغَيْرِ عِلْمٍ وَلَا هُدًى وَلَا كِتَابٍ مُنِيرٍ. لِيُضِلَّ عَن سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ لَهُ فِي الدُّنْيَا خِزْيٌ وَنُذِيقَهُ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ عَذَابَ الحريق﴾.
وقد عرف تاريخ الدعوة النبوية معاناة الرسل مع هذا النوع من الناس، وهم أكثر الخلق، إذ قابلهم هؤلاء بالمنازعة والجدل العنيف في الكثير من الأحيان، المصحوب بالأذى حين تعجزهم الحيل الفكرية والقولية. قال تعالى: ﴿وَمَا نُرْسِلُ الْمُرْسَلِينَ إِلَّا مُبَشِّرِينَ وَمُنذِرِينَ وَيُجَادِلُ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا بِالْبَاطِلِ لِيُدْحِضُوا بِهِ الْحَقَّ وَاتَّخَذُوا آيَاتِي وَمَا أُنذِرُوا هُزُوًا﴾. وقال عز وجل، ﴿مَا يُجَادِلُ فِي آيَاتِ اللهِ إِلَّا الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا فَلَا يَغْرُرُكَ تَقَلُّبُهُمْ فِي الْبِلَادِ كَذَّبَتْ قَبْلَهُمْ قَوْمُ نُوحٍ وَالْأَحْزَابُ مِنْ بَعْدِهِمْ وَهَمَّتْ كُلُّ أُمَّةٍ بِرَسُولِهِمْ﴾
The third demand: Man's disputation between truth and falsehood. Indeed, Allah's description of man as the most disputatious of things is evidence of the extent of his ability for intellectual trickery that enables him to argue with truth or falsehood, and to attack, retreat, and maneuver in argument. This ability has been available in man since the beginning of his existence on this earth, for he knew from his earliest formation how to parley and converse in speech and trained himself to argue with others. As a means through which he achieves his interests and persuades others to enable him to obtain those interests, through exchange or concession, and he did not refrain from using this means even to usurp and swallow the rights of others, let alone using it to obtain his legitimate rights. Human history bears witness that although man used argumentation for truth at times, as was the case of messengers, prophets, and preachers, he used it for falsehood most of the time, as most periods of history witnessed man's attempt to establish falsehood and suppress truth by adopting various tricks based on deception, fraud, evasion, and embellishment of speech with cunning and guile. The reason for man's victory of falsehood at the expense of truth in most cases is due to the domination of the inclinations of desire over his soul and their covering the outlets of his vision and insight, so that he sees only what his desire dictates even if it contains his destruction and ruin of his life. But strange in man's behavior is that when his uncontrolled desires and lusts push him to exceed the circle of truth, justice, goodness, and virtue, and he remains careful to appear before people in the guise of perfection, there arises in him an intense desire to prove the soundness of his conduct and the correctness of his method in life, so he resorts to the plan of embellishment and justification with falsehood, and if he encounters opposition or objection, he resorts to the plan of argumentation, and in argumentation he acts like a fighter desiring victory over his opponent, not careful to reach the truth through honorable and chaste debate. And although man usually knows what he hides in himself of eagerness to establish falsehood and deny truth, he still argues in the cause of falsehood, to repel heavy burdens from himself and follow desire which contains gratification of his pleasures and lusts. Allah has revealed this nature in man's soul, saying describing the deniers of resurrection who argue about it in denial and rejection, desiring to immerse themselves in the pleasures of worldly life: 'But man desires to persist in his sinful ways, asking, When is the Day of Resurrection?' So he denies the Last Day, and denies resurrection and gathering, not out of conviction that it will not happen, but to convince himself that what he indulges in of transgression, disobedience, and following desires and lusts is truth that should be followed and not deviated from, while he knows in the depths of his soul that it is falsehood that he should not indulge in. And Allah said: 'And among the people is he who disputes about Allah without knowledge and follows every rebellious devil.' And He said: 'And among the people is he who disputes about Allah without knowledge, without guidance, and without an enlightening book, to lead others astray from the way of Allah. For him in this world is disgrace, and on the Day of Resurrection We will make him taste the punishment of the burning fire.' The history of the prophetic call has known the suffering of the messengers with this type of people, who are the majority of creation, for these people confronted them with contention and violent argument many times, accompanied by harm when intellectual and verbal tricks fail them. Allah said: 'And We send the messengers only as bearers of good news and as warners. But those who disbelieve argue with falsehood to rebut the truth thereby, and they take My signs and that of which they are warned in mockery.' And He said: 'None dispute concerning the signs of Allah except those who disbelieve, so let not their striding about in the land delude you. The people of Noah denied before them, and the parties after them, and every nation plotted against their messenger.'
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is an exposition on the nature of human disputation (jadal), focusing on man's propensity to argue for falsehood. The author begins by stating that Allah's description of man as 'most disputatious' indicates his capacity for intellectual trickery, which he can use for either truth or falsehood. This ability has been present since the beginning of human existence. The author then notes that while man has used argumentation for truth (as prophets and preachers did), he more often uses it for falsehood, employing deception, evasion, and embellishment. The reason for this is the dominance of personal desires (hawa) over his soul, blinding him so that he only follows his whims even to his own destruction. Strangely, when desires push him beyond the bounds of truth, he still wants to appear perfect, so he justifies his actions with falsehood and, when opposed, resorts to argumentation like a fighter seeking victory, not truth. Even though he knows inwardly that he is defending falsehood, he continues to argue out of desire and to avoid burdens. The author then supports this with Quranic verses: verses about the deniers of resurrection who argue out of desire to continue sinning, and verses condemning those who dispute about Allah without knowledge, following devils, to mislead others. Finally, the author references the history of prophets who suffered from such people who argued violently and harmed them when intellectual tricks failed, citing Quranic verses that describe the disbelievers arguing with falsehood to rebut the truth and taking Allah's signs in mockery.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the purpose of the disbelievers' argumentation as described in the verse 'None dispute concerning the signs of Allah except those who disbelieve'?
A) To seek knowledge of truth.
B) To argue out of desire and to mislead.
C) To impress others with their eloquence.
D) To defend their faith sincerely.

Key Takeaway
The Quran exposes disputation for falsehood as a tool of those who follow desires and seek to mislead.

Dialectic -- Jadal
beginner
10 min
Blameworthy Jadal: Motive and Qur'anic Examples
Author describes blameworthy jadal motivated by desire and defends falsehood, citing Qur'anic examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify blameworthy jadal in a debate by distinguishing its motivation (desire for victory over truth) and recognize its pattern in Qur'anic narratives.

Core Idea
Blameworthy jadal is argumentation driven by desire, not truth.

In Islamic tradition, not all argumentation is equal. This lesson draws a sharp line between praiseworthy disputation seeking truth and blameworthy jadal motivated by ego and desire. Using powerful Qur'anic examples, you will learn to detect the telltale signs of the latter—arguments that defend falsehood and reject clear proofs out of stubbornness and lust.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of blameworthy jadal
Locate the opening sentence describing the arguer's motive: he desires victory, not truth. Note the terms 'راغبًا بالانتصار' and 'لا حريصًا على الوصول إلى الحق'.
2
Distinguish the inner motivation
The passage explains that the blameworthy arguer knows inwardly that he defends falsehood but continues to follow desire. Look for phrases like 'حرص على إقرار الباطل' and 'دفعا للتكاليف الثقيلة'.
3
Analyze the first Qur'anic example
Examine the verse from Surah al-Qiyamah (75:5-6) about deniers of resurrection. Notice that their denial is not intellectual but a pretext to continue sin. How does the author interpret this?
4
Trace the pattern across prophetic history
The author lists multiple prophets (Nuh, Hud, Salih, etc.) whose people argued with falsehood. Identify the common elements: rejection of clear proofs, violence when arguments fail, and ultimate divine punishment.
The consistent pattern is that every nation argued with their prophet 'liyudhiḍū bihi al-ḥaqq' (to refute the truth).

الجدل

راغبًا بالانتصار على خصمه لا حريصًا على الوصول إلى الحق بالمناظرة الشريفة العفيفة.
ومع أن الإنسان في العادة يعلم بما يخفيه في نفسه من حرص على إقرار الباطل والتنكر للحق، يظل مع ذلك يجادل في سبيل الباطل، دفعا للتكاليف الثقيلة عن نفسه واتباعًا للهوى الذي فيه إشباع لملذاته وشهواته وقد كشف الله عز وجل عن هذه الطبيعة في نفس الإنسان، فقال يصف منكري البعث الذين يجادلون فيه جحودا وإنكارا، رغبة في الاستغراق في متع الحياة الدنيا: ﴿بَل يُرِيدُ الإِنسَانُ لِيَفْجُرَ أَمَامَهُ يَسْأَلُ أَيَّانَ يَوْمُ الْقِيَامَةِ﴾، فهو ينكر اليوم الآخر، وينكر البعث والنشور لا اقتناعا بأن ذلك لن يكون، وإنما لكي يقنع نفسه بأن ما يخوض فيه من فسوق وعصيان وانسياق وراء الأهواء والشهوات حق ينبغي اتباعه وعدم الانحراف عنه، مع أنه يدرك في قرارة نفسه أنه باطل لا يجوز له الخوض فيه، وقال الله تعالى: ﴿وَمِنَ النَّاسِ مَن يُجَادِلُ فِي اللَّهِ بِغَيْرِ عِلْمٍ وَيَتَّبِعُ كُلَّ شَيْطَانٍ مَرِيدٍ﴾، وقال: ﴿وَمِنَ النَّاسِ مَن يُجَادِلُ فِي اللَّهِ بِغَيْرِ عِلْمٍ وَلَا هُدًى وَلَا كِتَابٍ مُنِيرٍ ثَانِيَ عِطْفِهِ لِيُضِلَّ عَن سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ لَهُ فِي الدُّنْيَا خِزْيٌ وَنُذِيقَهُ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ عَذَابَ الْحَرِيقِ﴾.
وقد عرف تاريخ الدعوة النبوية معاناة الرسل مع هذا النوع من الناس، وهم أكثر الخلق، إذ قابلهم هؤلاء بالمنازعة والجدل العنيف في الكثير من الأحيان، المصحوب بالأذى حين تعجزهم الحيل الفكرية والقولية. قال تعالى: ﴿وَمَا نُرْسِلُ الْمُرْسَلِينَ إِلَّا مُبَشِّرِينَ وَمُنذِرِينَ وَيُجَادِلُ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا بِالْبَاطِلِ لِيُدْحِضُوا بِهِ الْحَقَّ وَاتَّخَذُوا آيَاتِي وَمَا أُنذِرُوا هُزُوًا﴾. وقال عز وجل: ﴿مَا يُجَادِلُ فِي آيَاتِ اللَّهِ إِلَّا الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا فَلَا يَغْرُرْكَ تَقَلُّبُهُمْ فِي الْبِلَادِ كَذَّبَتْ قَبْلَهُمْ قَوْمُ نُوحٍ وَالْأَحْزَابُ مِنْ بَعْدِهِمْ وَهَمَّتْ كُلُّ أُمَّةٍ بِرَسُولِهِمْ لِيَأْخُذُوهُ وَجَادَلُوا بِالْبَاطِلِ لِيُدْحِضُوا بِهِ الْحَقَّ فَأَخَذْتُهُمْ فَكَيْفَ كَانَ عِقَابِ﴾. فدل هذا النص على أن كل أمة همت برسولهم ليأخذوه، وأن كل أمة جادلوا رسولهم بالباطل ليدحضوا به الحق، فقوم إبراهيم جادلوه في ربه، كما أن قوم شعيب جادلوه كذلك، وأما ثمود فجادلوا نبيهم صالحًا، وجادل قوم نوح نبيهم نوحا، كما جادلت عاد نبيهم هودا، ودار الجدل كذلك بين لوط وقومه فيما كانوا عليه من فواحش ومنكرات، وجادل فرعون وقومه رسول الله موسى، كما جادله بنو إسرائيل من بعد. وقد لخص القرآن الكريم كل هذه المجادلات في بضع آيات، فقال سبحانه وتعالى: ﴿أَلَمْ يَأْتِكُمْ نَبَأُ الَّذِينَ مِن قَبْلِكُمْ قَوْمِ نُوحٍ وَعَادٍ وَثَمُودَ وَالَّذِينَ مِن بَعْدِهِمْ لَا يَعْلَمُهُمْ إِلَّا اللَّهُ جَاءَتْهُمْ رُسُلُهُم بِالْبَيِّنَاتِ فَرَدُّوا أَيْدِيَهُمْ فِي أَفْوَاهِهِمْ وَقَالُوا إِنَّا كَفَرْنَا بِمَا أُرْسِلْتُم بِهِ وَإِنَّا لَفِي شَكٍّ مِّمَّا تَدْعُونَنَا إِلَيْهِ مُرِيبٍ قَالَتْ رُسُلُهُمْ أَفِي اللَّهِ شَكٌّ فَاطِرِ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ يَدْعُوكُمْ لِيَغْفِرَ لَكُم مِّن ذُنُوبِكُمْ وَيُؤَخِّرَكُمْ إِلَى أَجَلٍ مُّسَمًّى﴾
Dialectic

Desiring victory over his opponent, not eager to reach the truth through noble and chaste disputation. And although a person ordinarily knows what he conceals within himself of eagerness to affirm falsehood and disavow the truth, he nevertheless continues to argue in the way of falsehood, to repel heavy obligations from himself and to follow desire which contains the gratification of his pleasures and lusts. Allah, Mighty and Majestic, has revealed this nature in the soul of man. He said, describing the deniers of the resurrection who argue about it out of stubbornness and denial, desiring to immerse themselves in the pleasures of this worldly life: "Rather, man desires to continue in wickedness before him. He asks, 'When is the Day of Resurrection?'" So he denies the Last Day, and denies the resurrection and gathering, not out of conviction that it will not be, but rather to convince himself that his indulgence in immorality, disobedience, and following desires and lusts is right and should be followed and not deviated from, even though he knows in the depths of his soul that it is false and not permissible for him to engage in. And Allah Almighty said: "And among the people is he who argues about Allah without knowledge and follows every rebellious devil." And He said: "And among the people is he who argues about Allah without knowledge, nor guidance, nor an enlightening scripture, turning away his neck to lead away from the way of Allah. For him in this world is disgrace, and We will make him taste on the Day of Resurrection the punishment of the burning fire."

The history of the prophetic call has known the suffering of the messengers with this type of people, who are the majority of creation. They met them with conflict and violent argument on many occasions, accompanied by harm when intellectual and verbal tricks failed them. He said, the Exalted: "And We do not send the messengers except as bringers of good tidings and warners. And those who disbelieve argue with falsehood to refute the truth thereby. And they take My verses and that of which they are warned in ridicule." And He, Mighty and Majestic, said: "No one argues about the verses of Allah except those who disbelieve. So let not their movement in the lands deceive you. The people of Noah denied before them, and the factions after them, and every nation intended [harm] for their messenger to seize him, and they argued with falsehood to refute the truth thereby. So I seized them. And how [terrible] was My punishment." Thus this text indicates that every nation intended [harm] for their messenger to seize him, and that every nation argued with their messenger with falsehood to refute the truth thereby. So the people of Abraham argued with him about his Lord, as did the people of Shu'ayb. As for Thamud, they argued with their prophet Salih. And the people of Noah argued with their prophet Noah. And 'Ad argued with their prophet Hud. And argument also took place between Lot and his people concerning what they were upon of lewdness and evils. And Pharaoh and his people argued with the messenger of Allah, Moses, as did the Children of Israel after him. And the Noble Qur'an has summarized all these arguments in a few verses. He, the Exalted, said: "Has there not come to you the news of those before you: the people of Noah and 'Ad and Thamud and those after them? None knows them but Allah. Their messengers came to them with clear proofs, but they thrust their hands into their mouths and said, 'Indeed, we disbelieve in that with which you have been sent, and indeed we are in disquieting doubt about that to which you invite us.' Their messengers said, 'Can there be doubt about Allah, Creator of the heavens and earth? He invites you that He may forgive you of your sins and delay you for a specified term.'"
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of blameworthy jadal (argumentation) in the Islamic tradition. It begins by describing the motive of such argumentation: the arguer seeks victory over his opponent, not truth, and is driven by an inward desire to affirm falsehood and reject truth, in order to escape heavy obligations and follow base desires. The author then cites several Qur'anic verses to illustrate this nature. First, from Surah al-Qiyamah, describing those who deny the resurrection because they want to continue in sin; they ask mockingly about the Day of Judgment not out of doubt but to justify their wrongdoing. Next, from Surah al-Hajj, verses highlighting those who argue about Allah without knowledge, following devils, and turning away arrogantly to lead others astray. The author then explains that prophets historically faced this type of people, who engaged in violent argument and harm when intellectual arguments failed. He cites Surah al-Kahf and Surah Ghafir, which describe disbelievers arguing with falsehood to refute truth, and the fate of past nations. The passage then enumerates specific examples from the Qur'an: the people of Abraham, Shu'ayb, Salih, Noah, Hud, and Lot; also Pharaoh and the Children of Israel arguing with Moses. Finally, it summarizes a longer verse from Surah Ibrahim that encapsulates the response of many nations: they rejected the clear proofs of their messengers with stubbornness and doubt, while the messengers affirmed that there is no doubt about Allah, the Creator. The author uses these examples to show that jadal in defense of falsehood is a recurring historical phenomenon, condemned in the Qur'an.

باطل
مناظرة

Three Categories of Qur'anic Audience and Their Methods
Author classifies people into three types based on how they are addressed in the Qur'an.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the three types of Qur'anic audience and identify which method (burhan, jadal, or rhetoric) is appropriate for each.

Core Idea
The Qur'an uses three methods—demonstration, dialectic, and rhetoric—each tailored to a different audience.

In this passage, the author explains that Allah diversified the methods of address in the Qur'an to suit the varied natures of people. Some are convinced by pure demonstration, others need dialectical argument using their own premises, and the majority respond to rhetorical appeal. Understanding this classification helps us appreciate the Qur'an's comprehensive approach to guidance and the legitimacy of different methods of persuasion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three groups
Read the Arabic passage and note the three categories: (a) those who accept only demonstration (burhan), (b) those dominated by partisan doctrine needing dialectic (jadal), and (c) the common majority addressed by rhetoric (maw'izah hasanah).
2
Match each group with its method
For group (a), the method is burhan (complete syllogism). For group (b), it is jadal (dialectical argument using opponent's premises). For group (c), it is maw'izah hasanah (good exhortation) and wisdom.
The verse 16:125 is cited as the command for the Prophet to use these methods.
3
Understand the rationale
The author explains that people's natures differ: the few rationalists require strict proof; the fanatically partisan need a method that engages their own commitments; the majority are best reached by appealing to their innate fitra with eloquent truth.
This reflects the Islamic principle of addressing people according to their understanding (mukhatabah 'ala qadr 'uqulihim).
4
Apply the classification to a real example
Consider the Qur'an's approach to polytheists: sometimes it uses demonstration (e.g., arguments for tawhid), sometimes dialectic (e.g., challenging their beliefs using their own logic), and sometimes rhetoric (e.g., descriptions of paradise and hell). Identify which method fits which audience type.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تمهید: أنزل الله عز وجل القرآن الكريم إلى عباده، مخاطبًا إياهم من خلاله، داعيًا لهم إلى الإيمان به وعبادته والخضوع لأوامره والانتهاء عن نواهيه، ومن البديهي أن يخاطب الله سبحانه وتعالى عباده بما يفهمونه ويدركونه من أساليب القول وصيغ التعبير، كما كان من البديهي أيضًا أن ينوع لهم الخطاب ووسائل التبليغ، فإن لم تنفع معهم طريقة ربما نفعت طريقة أو طرق أخرى، إضافة إلى أن الناس ليسوا كلهم سواء في الفهم والاقتناع، إذ أن طبائعهم متفاوتة، ومشاربهم مختلفة، وأهواءهم متنازعة ومسالكهم في طلب الحق متعددة : أ - فمنهم من يصدق بالبرهان، ولا يرضيه إلا قياس تام أو ما يجري مجراه، وهؤلاء هم من غلبت عليهم النزعات العقلية والتأملات الفلسفية، وهؤلاء في الأمم قلة من الناس، وعددهم محدود بالنسبة إلى غيرهم، إذ أن أكثر من في الأرض قد انصرف إلى المهن من زراعة وصناعة، فما كان له من وقت يزجيه في تلك التأملات، ولهذا أمر الله تعالى نبيه أن يدعو إليه بالحكمة في قوله تعالى : ﴿وادْعُ إِلَى سَبِيلِ رَبِّكَ بِالْحِكْمَةِ وَالْمَوْعِظَةِ الْحَسَنَةِ وَجَادِلْهُم بِالَّتِي هِيَ أَحْسَنُ﴾. ب - ومن الناس من غلب عليه مذهب ديني أو غير ديني قد استأثر بلبه، وسد مسام الإدراك، إذ استولت عليه نحلة مذهبية فتعصب لها، والتعصب يعمي ويصم، ويجعل النفس لا تستسيغ الحق إلا بمعالجات عسيرة، وإن الإقناع بذلك لا يكون إلا بالطب لأدواء النفوس، وأدواء النفوس أعسر علاجا، وأعز دواء من علاج الأجسام . وهؤلاء لابد لهم من طريق جدلية تزيل ما لبس الحق عليهم، ويتخذ بها قوة مما يعتقدون، إذ يلزمهم بما عندهم ويفحصهم بما بين أيديهم، ويتخذ مما يعرفون وسيلة لإلزامهم بما يرفضون. ج - وهو الجمهور الأعظم من الناس فليسوا هؤلاء، ولا أولئك، بل هو في تفكيره أقرب إلى الفطرة فيه سلامتها، وفيه سذاجتها، وفيه إخلاصها وبراءتها، لا يخاطب بتفكير الفلاسفة، ولا يخاطب بما يخاطب به المتفكرون تفكرًا علميًا، بل يليق به ما التقى فيه الحق مع مخاطبة الوجدان، وما التقت فيه اليقينية بما يجعل الأهواء تابعة لها والميول خاضعة لمنهاجها وما التقت فيه سلاسة البيان وبلاغة قوة الحق وليس بما يختص به أهل المنطق، ولا ما عليه أهل العلوم الكونية، إنما يخاطب الجمهور الأعظم بالحق وبما يغذي الفطرة وبما يثيرها ويوجهها إلى السبيل الأقوم. فالقرآن الكريم استعمل كل الأساليب التي تليق بمخاطبة كل صنف من هذه الأصناف ومنها : أسلوب الجدل والحوار الفكري المقرون بالأدلة العقلية والشواهد والحجج الواقعية.
Introduction: Allah the Exalted sent down the Holy Qur'an to His servants, addressing them through it, calling them to believe in Him, worship Him, submit to His commands, and refrain from His prohibitions. It is self-evident that Allah addresses His servants with what they understand and comprehend from styles of speech and forms of expression. It was also self-evident that He diversified for them the discourse and means of communication. If one method does not benefit them, perhaps another method or other methods will benefit, in addition to the fact that people are not all equal in understanding and conviction, because their natures are varied, their inclinations different, their desires conflicting, and their paths in seeking truth manifold: a) Among them are those who believe through demonstration (burhan) and are satisfied only with a complete syllogism (qiyas tamm) or what runs its course. These are those in whom rational tendencies and philosophical reflections dominate. These among nations are few in number, and their count is limited relative to others, for most people on earth are occupied with professions of agriculture and industry, having no time to spend in such reflections. For this reason Allah commanded His Prophet to call to Him with wisdom in His saying: 'Call to the way of your Lord with wisdom and good exhortation, and debate with them in the best manner.' b) Among people are those in whom a religious or non-religious doctrine dominates, having taken possession of their heart and blocked the channels of perception. A partisan school has taken hold of them and they become fanatical about it. Fanaticism blinds and deafens, and makes the soul not accept the truth except through difficult treatments. Persuasion in that case can only be through medicine for the diseases of souls, and the diseases of souls are harder to treat and rarer in remedy than bodily diseases. These people must have a dialectical method (tariq jadaliyya) that removes the confusion of truth from them, and through it they gain strength from what they believe. It binds them by their own beliefs, examines them by what is in their hands, and uses what they know as a means to oblige them to what they reject. c) The vast majority of people are neither these nor those, but their thinking is closer to innate nature (fitra) in its soundness, simplicity, sincerity, and purity. They are not addressed with the thinking of philosophers nor with the thinking of those who ponder scientifically. Rather, what suits them is where truth meets the appeal to conscience, where certainty makes passions subservient and desires submit to its path, and where smoothness of expression and eloquence of the power of truth meet, not what is specific to logicians nor what the scholars of natural sciences adhere to. Rather, the vast majority is addressed with truth, with what nourishes the innate nature, stirs it, and directs it to the straightest path. Thus the Holy Qur'an used all the methods suitable for addressing each of these types, including the method of dialectic (jadal) and intellectual dialogue coupled with rational proofs, evidences, and real arguments.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is an introduction (tamhid) that classifies the recipients of Qur'anic discourse into three categories and explains the appropriate method for each. The author begins by stating that Allah addresses people in ways they can understand, and naturally varies these methods because people differ in comprehension and conviction. Then three categories are delineated: (a) Those who require demonstration (burhan) – rational proofs like complete syllogisms. They are few, mostly philosophers and intellectuals. For them, Allah commanded the Prophet to call with wisdom (hikma), referring to verse 16:125. (b) Those dominated by partisan adherence (madhhab) that blinds them. They need a dialectical method (tariq jadaliyya) that uses their own beliefs to lead them to truth, like a doctor treating spiritual diseases. (c) The common majority (al-jumhur al-a'zam) – people of sound fitra, not given to deep speculation. They are addressed with rhetoric that appeals to conscience and stirs innate nature. The Qur'an therefore employs all these styles, including jadal (dialectic) as one of them. The commentary then flows: the author's point is that jadal is a legitimate and necessary method for certain audiences, not inferior to burhan but appropriate for those entrenched in partisanship. The threefold division mirrors classical Islamic thought on audience adaptation (e.g., Ibn Rushd's distinction in Fasl al-Maqal). All examples cited are from the Qur'an itself.

Key Terms
البرهان
الجدل
الموعظة الحسنة
القياس التام

Frequency of the Jadal Root in the Qur'an
Author enumerates occurrences of the root j-d-l in the Qur'an with counts and references.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the number of occurrences of the root j-d-l in the Qur'an and differentiate between its simple and augmented verbal forms.

Core Idea
Jadal is not marginal but appears 29 times in 27 Qur'anic verses.

Before diving into the rules of jadal (dialectic), it is essential to establish that the practice has a firm Qur'anic foundation. This passage from our text enumerates every occurrence of the root j-d-l in the Qur'an, counting 29 instances across 27 verses. By learning this, you will appreciate that debate and argumentation are not foreign to Islam but are woven into the divine discourse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the root under study
The passage focuses on the root letters j-d-l (ج د ل). Recognise that this is the lexical foundation for words related to argumentation and debate.
2
Note the total count
The author explicitly states that the root appears 29 times. Commit this number to memory, as it is often cited to show the Qur'anic emphasis on jadal.
3
Distinguish simple from augmented forms
Two instances are in the simple verbal noun (masdar mujarrad) form, while the remaining 27 are in augmented forms such as 'jadala' (past, present, imperative) and the verbal noun 'jidal'. Understand that the augmented forms indicate a more intense or reciprocal action.
4
Locate the verses
The passage lists 27 specific verses. Take note of the range: from Al-Baqarah to Al-Mujadala. This shows that jadal spans both Meccan and Medinan periods.
You may look up any of the verses, e.g., Al-Nahl 125, which commands to 'argue in the best way'.
5
Grasp the purpose of the enumeration
The author's aim is to demonstrate that jadal is a legitimate and recurring theme in the Qur'an, thus providing scriptural support for the discipline of jadal itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المطلب الأول : مادة الجدل في القرآن الكريم ورد أصل كلمة (ج د ل) في القرآن تسعة وعشرين مرة بصيغها المختلفة أي : مرتين بصيغة المصدر من المجرد والبقية بصيغة المزيد بحرف، «جادل» بأزمانها الثلاثة وبأحد مصدريها «جدال»، كل ذلك في سبع وعشرين آية، وقد ذكر الآيات : البقرة 197، النساء 107، 109، الأنعام 25، 121، الأعراف 71، الأنفال 6، هود 32، 74، الرعد 13، النحل 125، 54، الكهف 56، الحج 8، 68، العنكبوت 46، لقمان 20، غافر 4، 5، 35، 56، الشورى 35، الزخرف 58، المجادلة 1.
The first sub-topic: The material of jadal in the Holy Qur'an. The root word (j-d-l) appears in the Qur'an twenty-nine times in its various forms: i.e., twice in the form of the verbal noun (masdar) of the simple verb, and the rest in the form of the augmented verb with a letter, 'jadala' in its three tenses and one of its two verbal nouns 'jidal', all in twenty-seven verses. And he mentioned the verses: Al-Baqarah 197, Al-Nisa 107, 109, Al-An'am 25, 121, Al-A'raf 71, Al-Anfal 6, Hud 32, 74, Al-Ra'd 13, Al-Nahl 125, 54, Al-Kahf 56, Al-Hajj 8, 68, Al-'Ankabut 46, Luqman 20, Ghafir 4, 5, 35, 56, Al-Shura 35, Al-Zukhruf 58, Al-Mujadala 1.

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of the occurrences of the root j-d-l in the Qur'an, establishing its prominence. The author states that the root occurs 29 times in 27 verses, specifying that two instances are the simple verbal noun (masdar mujarrad) while the rest are in augmented forms (mazid biharf) like 'jadala' in past, present, and imperative, and the verbal noun 'jidal'. A list of 27 verse references follows. The author's purpose is to show that jadal is not marginal but a recurrent theme in the Qur'an, supporting its legitimacy as a method of debate and argumentation. The verses are cited from various Meccan and Medinan surahs, indicating the wide applicability of the practice.
