Three Audiences of Jadal: Methods for Each
Author describes the second and third categories of people addressed by jadal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three categories of people addressed by jadal and identify the appropriate argumentation method for each based on their intellectual and spiritual disposition.

Core Idea
Jadal adapts its method to the audience: philosophers, scriptuaries, and the general public each require a distinct approach.

In the previous lesson, the author introduced the first category of people in jadal—the intellectuals and philosophers. Now he turns to the second and third categories: the People of the Book and the general public. Understanding these categories is crucial for applying the correct method of argumentation, as each group has a different capacity and requires a different rhetorical and logical strategy. The author grounds his classification in both Quranic injunction and human nature (fitra).

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
From the passage and context, list the three types of people: 1) those with intellectual/philosophical thinking (mentioned earlier), 2) the People of the Book (Ahl al-Kitab), 3) the general public (al-jumhur al-a'zam). Note the Quranic verse that guides the approach for the second category.
The first category is not described in this chunk but is implied from the broader lesson.
2
Understand the method for the People of the Book
The author quotes the Quran: 'Do not argue with the People of the Book except in the best way.' This means using gentleness, respect, and the best possible arguments, avoiding harshness or provocation.
The 'best way' (allati hiya ahsan) is a Quranic principle for interfaith dialogue.
3
Analyze the characteristics of the general public
The general public is described as being close to fitra—innate, sound, simple, sincere, and innocent. They are not addressed with philosophical or scientific reasoning, but with truth that appeals to conscience and emotion, and that nourishes the fitra.
The term 'fitra' here includes both moral intuition and natural receptivity to truth.
4
Contrast the methods for each category
Compare: the first category (intellectuals) require logical proofs and philosophical arguments; the second category (People of the Book) require the best, most respectful argument; the third category (general public) require an approach that combines truth with emotional appeal and simplicity.
The author explicitly excludes logic and natural science methods for the general public.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا الصنف من الناس وإن كان أكثر عددًا من الأول، ليس هو الجمهور الأعظم ولا الكثرة الغالبة بين الناس، ولعله الذي أمرنا الله تعالى بألا نجادله إلا أحسن، وذلك في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا تُجَادِلُوا أَهْلَ الْكِتَابِ إِلَّا بِالَّتِي هِيَ أَحْسَنُ﴾(1). وأما الجمهور الأعظم من الناس فليسوا هؤلاء، ولا أولئك، بل هو في تفكيره أقرب إلى الفطرة فيه سلامتها، وفيه سذاجتها، وفيه إخلاصها وبراءتها، لا يخاطب بتفكير الفلاسفة، ولا يخاطب بما يخاطب به المتفكرون تفكرًا علميًا، بل يليق به ما التقى فيه الحق مع مخاطبة الوجدان، وما التقت فيه اليقينية بما يجعل الأهواء تابعة لها والميول خاضعة لمنهاجها وما التقت فيه سلاسة البيان وبلاغة قوة الحق وليس بما يختص به أهل المنطق، ولا ما عليه أهل العلوم الكونية، إنما يخاطب الجمهور الأعظم بالحق وبما يغذي الفطرة وبما يثيرها ويوجهها إلى السبيل الأقوم(2)
And this category of people, even if they are more numerous than the first, are not the general public nor the overwhelming majority among people. Perhaps they are the ones whom Allah commanded us not to argue with except in the best way, as in His saying: 'And do not argue with the People of the Book except in the best way.' As for the general public among people, they are neither these nor those, but rather in their thinking they are closer to innate nature (fitra) with its soundness, its simplicity, its sincerity and innocence. They are not addressed with the thinking of philosophers, nor with what scientific thinkers address, but rather what suits them is where truth meets addressing the conscience, and where certainty meets making desires follow it and inclinations submit to its path, and where fluency of expression and eloquence of the power of truth meet, and not what is specific to the people of logic, nor what the people of natural sciences have. Rather, the general public is addressed with truth and with what nourishes the fitra and what provokes it and guides it to the straightest path.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage defines the second and third categories of people in the context of dialectical argument (jadal). The author begins by referring to the second category, who are more numerous than the first category (which was presumably the philosophers or intellectuals). They are commanded to be argued with in the best manner, as per the Quranic verse. Then the author describes the third category, the general public (al-jumhur al-a'zam), who are not like the first two. They are closer to innate nature (fitra)—simple, sincere, and innocent. They are not addressed with philosophical or scientific reasoning. Instead, the appropriate method for them combines truth with appeal to conscience, certainty with controlling desires, and eloquent expression. This method is not that of logicians or scientists. The general public is addressed directly with truth and nourishment of the fitra. This classification is crucial for understanding the different audiences in Islamic dialectic.

الجمهور الأعظم
الفطرة

Key Takeaway
Jadal is not a one-size-fits-all method; the audience's intellectual capacity and disposition determine the appropriate argumentative approach.

Jadal in the Quran: Root, Statistics, and Meccan/Medinan Distribution
Author surveys the root j-d-l in the Quran, its frequency, and the prominence of jadal in Meccan versus Medinan verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the root occurrences of jadal in the Quran and explain why the Meccan period emphasized jadal more than the Medinan period.

Core Idea
Jadal in the Quran goes beyond the root letters; it is a core method of persuasion, especially in Meccan verses.

This lesson examines the Quran's use of jadal. We will first look at the linguistic statistics of the root j-d-l, then explore the broader presence of jadal as a method, and finally understand why the Meccan revelation prioritized jadal against polytheists.

Guided Path
1
Identify the root and its occurrences
The root j-d-l appears in 27 verses, with 29 occurrences in various forms (masdar, verb, etc.). Notice that the word itself is limited in frequency.
2
Distinguish the root from the method
The author argues that jadal as a method of argumentation pervades the Quran far beyond the 27 verses. The Quran is described as a 'book of jadal about creed and law.'
3
Compare Meccan vs. Medinan focus
17 Meccan verses mention jadal explicitly, indicating a greater emphasis in the Meccan period. The Medinan period also contains jadal but focused more on People of the Book.
4
Explain theological reasons for Meccan emphasis
The Meccan period needed to establish tawhid, prophethood, and the afterlife, requiring strong proofs and debates against polytheists. The passage lists moral and material obstacles that necessitated jadal.

فالقرآن الكريم استعمل كل الأساليب التي تليق بمخاطبة كل صنف الأصناف ومنها؛ أسلوب الجدل والحوار الفكري المقرون بالأدلة العقلية والشواهد والحجج الواقعية. المطلب الأول : مادة الجدل في القرآن الكريم ورد أصل كلمة (ج د، ل) في القرآن تسعة وعشرين مرة بصيغها المختلفة أي : مرتين بصيغة المصدر من المجرد والبقية بصيغة المزيد بحرف، «جادل» بأزمانها الثلاثة وبأحد مصدريها «جدال»، كل ذلك في سبع وعشرين آية»(3)، وقد حث الله المسلمين في هذه الآيات المتعددة، إخبارًا وأمرًا، على مجادلة أهل الكتاب والكفار على حد سواء، وذلك رجاء إرجاعهم إلى الطريق السوي والصراط المستقيم (1) . والواقع أن مادة الجدل في القرآن الكريم لا تتوقف عند هذا العدد المحدود من الآيات، بل إنها تنساب في سور القرآن الكريم كلها، صحيح أن المادة اللغوية (ج) ، د ، ل لا تذكر إلا في هذه المرات المذكورة، إلا أن الجدل كمادة فكرية أو كمنهج، موجود بكثرة في القرآن الكريم، حتى إننا نكاد نقول إن القرآن هو كتاب جدل عن العقيدة والشريعة . ولربما كانت المرحلة المكية من نزول القرآن أكثر احتفالا بالجدل كأسلوب في خطاب الكفار والمشركين، حيث اختص العهد المكي بسبع عشرة آية تعرضت لذكر الجدل، وذلك لأن طبيعة هذه المرحلة بالذات وما تميزت به من مقاصد أساسية تود الدعوة إثباتها وترسيخها، تستلزم إثارة الموضوع قصدًا أو عرضًا، فعقيدة التوحيد يتطلب تأسيسها إقامة الشواهد المثبتة وادعاء النبوة يفرض التصديق به تقديم المؤيدات المقنعة، والإيمان باليوم الآخر يتوقف قبوله على إبانة الحجج القاطعة، بالإضافة إلى أن هناك عوائق معنوية متمكنة يقتضي اقتلاعها عقد مناظرات مفحمة وعراقيل مادية متحكمة يحتم تضييق الخناق عليها تنظيم محاورات ومناقشات تبكيتية»(2) ولا يعني هذا أن المرحلة المدنية قد خلت من الطابع الجدلي، بل إنها حفلت الأخرى بمجادلة اليهود والنصارى، لكن بشكل أقل مما حدث مع المشركين في المرحلة المكية التي كان التركيز فيها منصبا على غرس العقيدة وإثباتها بمختلف الوسائل الإقناعية .. وقد استقرأ الإمام نجم الدين الطوفي نماذج الجدل في القرآن الكريم، فعرض علينا عشرات الصور الجدلية من أكثر من خمسين سورة من سور القرآن الكريم مكية ومدنية على سواء، كما تبين من استقراء ما(3)
The Holy Quran used all methods suitable for addressing each category of people, including the method of jadal and intellectual dialogue coupled with rational proofs, evidences, and real arguments. First topic: The material of jadal in the Holy Quran. The root of the word (j-d-l) appears in the Quran twenty-nine times in its various forms, i.e., twice in the form of the simple masdar and the rest in the form of the augmented verb with a letter, 'jadala' in its three tenses and one of its two masdars 'jidal', all of which in twenty-seven verses. Allah has urged the Muslims in these multiple verses, informing and commanding, to argue with the People of the Book and the disbelievers alike, in hopes of returning them to the right path and straight path. In reality, the material of jadal in the Holy Quran does not stop at this limited number of verses, but rather it flows through all the chapters of the Holy Quran. True, the linguistic material (j-d-l) is only mentioned in these mentioned times, but jadal as an intellectual material or as a method exists abundantly in the Holy Quran, to the point that we almost say that the Quran is a book of jadal about creed and law. Perhaps the Meccan period of the revelation of the Quran was more celebratory of jadal as a method in addressing the disbelievers and polytheists, as the Meccan period was distinguished by seventeen verses that addressed jadal. This is because the nature of this period itself and its fundamental objectives that the da'wa wanted to prove and consolidate necessitated raising the subject intentionally or incidentally. The creed of tawhid requires establishing proofs for its foundation, the claim of prophethood imposes presenting convincing evidence for belief in it, and faith in the Last Day depends on presenting conclusive proofs. Additionally, there are deep-rooted moral obstacles that require holding devastating debates, and controlling material obstacles that necessitate organizing humiliating discussions. This does not mean that the Medinan period was devoid of jadal, but rather it was full of arguing with Jews and Christians, but to a lesser extent than with the polytheists in the Meccan period, which focused on implanting the creed and proving it through various persuasive means. Imam Najm al-Din al-Tufi surveyed the examples of jadal in the Holy Quran, and presented dozens of jadal forms from more than fifty chapters of the Quran, both Meccan and Medinan alike, as shown from his survey.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage examines the presence of jadal in the Quran. It first states that the Quran uses all methods, including jadal. Then under the heading 'Material of Jadal in the Quran,' the author provides linguistic statistics: the root j-d-l appears 29 times in various forms, but in 27 verses. Allah commands Muslims to argue with both People of the Book and disbelievers. The passage then argues that jadal as a method is pervasive in the Quran beyond these verses. The author highlights that the Meccan period, with 17 verses mentioning jadal, was particularly focused on jadal against polytheists due to the need to establish tawhid, prophethood, and the afterlife, and to overcome obstacles. The Medinan period also had jadal but focused on Jews and Christians. Finally, al-Tufi's work is referenced as a comprehensive collection of jadal examples from over fifty surahs.

Key Terms
مادة الجدل (maddat al-jadal): The linguistic material or content of jadal in the Quran, referring to the root letters and their occurrences.
العهد المكي (al-'ahd al-makki): The Meccan period of revelation, characterized by focus on jadal against polytheists.
العهد المدني (al-'ahd al-madani): The Medinan period, with jadal but more against Jews and Christians.

Key Takeaway
The Quran contains jadal both as a word and as a pervasive method, with Meccan verses heavily focusing on jadal to establish core beliefs.

Dialectic -- Jadal

Three Types of Jadal in the Qur'an
Author enumerates three types of jadal in the Qur'an with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify occurrences of jadal in the Qur'an into three types based on purpose and source, and identify examples of each.

Core Idea
Jadal in the Qur'an is not monolithic; it has legitimate, exploratory, and false forms.

When you open the Qur'an, you encounter debates: prophets with their people, believers with disbelievers, and even a prophet with his Lord. Are all of these arguments the same? The author of this passage says no—there are three distinct types. By learning this classification, you will be able to read these passages with a more discerning eye, recognizing the intention behind each dialectical exchange.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
The author explicitly states that jadal in the Qur'an appears in three forms. Find the Arabic terms or descriptions for each type in the passage.
The three types are: جَدَلٌ بِالْحَقِّ (argument with truth), exploratory dialogue (الاسترشاد وحب الاستطلاع), and جَدَلٌ بِالْبَاطِلِ (argument with falsehood).
2
Extract defining characteristics per type
For each type, note what the author says about its source, purpose, and method. For type A, it is from Allah and prophets to establish truth. Type B is for seeking reassurance or knowledge. Type C comes from disbelievers to refute truth.
The author contrasts the purpose: type A is for الإلزام والإفحام (compulsion and refutation) but also guidance; type B is for الطمأنينة (reassurance); type C is لِيُدْحِضُوا بِهِ الْحَقَّ (to refute truth).
3
Match the given examples
The author provides examples: Prophet Ibrahim's question, the angels' argument, Khawlah bint Tha'labah for type B; and disbelievers' objections for type C. Identify which example belongs to which type.
Ibrahim's dialogue with Allah is explicitly placed under type B, not type A, because it is exploratory, not confrontational.
4
Apply the classification to a new verse
Think of another Qur'anic debate, such as Moses with Pharaoh (Q. 20:49-55). Would you classify this as type A, B, or C? Justify using the passage's criteria.
This step prepares you for the application task.

ورد في القرآن الكريم من جدل بصوره المختلفة والمتنوعة ثلاثة أوجه :
— أنه ينحصر في الأدلة من «أ - ما الله رد به على الخصوم من الحجج والبراهين وما ساقه لتثبيت العقائد وتقرير قواعد الملة مما جاء على ألسنة رسله وأنبيائه وما ألهم به أمر عباده الصالحين من قول بالحق ودفع للباطل، وهذا جدل بالحق، بل هو ضروري لتبليغ رسالة الله إلى أهل الأرض ودفع ما يعتورها من شبهات وما يقف في طريقها من عقبات وكشف ما يحاك ضدها من مؤامرات وما يدبر لها من كيد وضلال، وهذا النوع من الجدل القرآني وإن كان فيه معنى الإلزام والإفحام إلا أنه مشتمل على التوجيه والإرشاد إلى طريق الحق والصواب.
ب — ما ورد في القرآن بطريق الحوار والقصد منه الاسترشاد وحب الاستطلاع والنظر للعظة والاعتبار أو الترجي والدعاء، ومن هذا القبيل جدل إبراهيم عليه السلام مع ربه، حيث قال : وَرَبِّ أَرِنِي كَيْفَ تُحْيِ الْمَوْتَى قَالَ أَوَلَمْ تُؤْمِن قَالَ بَلَى وَلَكِن لِيَطْمَئِنَّ قَلْبِي ...، وهكذا جدال الملائكة وجدال خولة بنت ثعلبة التي حكى الله قصتها في سورة المجادلة، ونحو ذلك مما يرجع إلى هذا المعنى .
ج - ما يأتي على ألسنة الكفار من الاعتراضات والشبه والدعاوى الباطلة التي حكاها القرآن الكريم وبين بطلانها وما تنطوي عليه من مفاسد، وهذا يدخل تحت عنوان الجدل بالباطل، كما قال تعالى : وَجَدَلُوا بِالْبَاطِلِ لِيُدْحِضُوا بِهِ الْحَقَّ .
There occur in the Noble Qur'an from argument (jadal) in its various and diverse forms three aspects: — (A) That which is confined to evidences: what Allah has refuted the opponents with, of proofs and demonstrations, and what He has brought to establish beliefs and settle the foundations of the religion, from what came on the tongues of His messengers and prophets, and what He inspired His righteous servants to say of truth and repel falsehood — this is argument with truth; indeed it is necessary for conveying Allah's message to the people of the earth and repelling the doubts that afflict it and the obstacles that stand in its way, and exposing the conspiracies woven against it and the plots devised for it of deception and misguidance. This type of Qur'anic argument, though it contains the sense of compulsion and refutation, yet it includes direction and guidance to the path of truth and right. (B) What occurs in the Qur'an by way of dialogue, its purpose being seeking guidance, love of inquiry, and looking for admonition and consideration, or hoping and supplication. Of this kind is the argument of Abraham, peace be upon him, with his Lord, when he said: 'My Lord, show me how You give life to the dead.' He said: 'Do you not believe?' He said: 'Yes, but that my heart may be assured.' And likewise the argument of the angels and the argument of Khawlah bint Tha'labah, whose story Allah related in Surat al-Mujadilah, and similar cases that revert to this meaning. (C) What comes on the tongues of the disbelievers of objections, doubts, and false claims that the Noble Qur'an has related and demonstrated their falsehood and the corruptions they entail. This falls under the heading of argument with falsehood, as the Exalted said: 'And they argued with falsehood to refute thereby the truth.'
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage classifies the occurrences of jadal (argumentation or debate) in the Qur'an into three distinct types. The author begins by stating that jadal appears in three forms. The first type (A) is 'jadal bil-haqq' (argument with truth). This is the argument conducted by Allah Himself or by His prophets and righteous servants to establish the faith and refute falsehood. It is characterized by compulsion (ilzam) and refutation (ifham), but its ultimate purpose is guidance and direction to the truth, not mere victory. The second type (B) is exploratory dialogue. This is not adversarial but rather a means of seeking knowledge, reassurance, or invoking Allah. The example of Prophet Ibrahim asking to see how Allah resurrects the dead illustrates this: his question was not out of disbelief but to increase certainty. The third type (C) is 'jadal bil-batil' (argument with falsehood), which comes from the disbelievers. The Qur'an narrates their objections only to refute them and expose their falsehood. Thus, the classification shows that jadal itself is neutral; its value depends on the intention and method. The author uses Qur'anic examples to ground the discussion in revelation, a common approach in Islamic dialectic works.

Key Terms
جدل
جدل بالحق
جدل بالباطل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of jadal does the example of Prophet Ibrahim (peace be upon him) asking to see the resurrection fall under?
A) Jadal bil-haqq, because it involves a prophet.
B) Jadal bil-batil, because it questions Allah's power.
C) The exploratory/dialogue type, because it seeks reassurance and guidance.
D) None of the above; it is a separate category.

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an contains three types of jadal: argument with truth (jadal bil-haqq), exploratory dialogue, and argument with falsehood (jadal bil-batil); each serves a different purpose.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Find another verse where a believer engages in dialogue with a disbeliever. Classify it and explain your reasoning based on the three types.

Purpose of Qur'anic Jadal and Ibn Taymiyya's Classification
Author explains the goal of Qur'anic jadal is guidance, then cites Ibn Taymiyya's three categories of people addressed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Qur'anic purpose of jadal (guidance) from mere disputation, and apply Ibn Taymiyya's tripartite classification to determine the appropriate method of engagement.

Core Idea
Qur'anic jadal is not winning an argument but guiding to truth with wisdom, admonition, or debate.

In this lesson, we explore the fundamental purpose of jadal in the Qur'an as presented by the author and grounded in Ibn Taymiyya's commentary. You will learn that the goal is not to defeat the opponent but to lead them to truth, using methods suited to their state of knowledge and action. The Qur'an models gentle argumentation and often defers final judgment to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overarching purpose of jadal in the Qur'an
The author states that jadal is a means to convince people of the Islamic creed and guide them to right action, not an end in itself or merely for confounding opponents.
2
Examine the Qur'anic method of arguing
The Qur'an argues gently, does not prolong debate to hostility, and often ends verses by deferring judgment to Allah, showing humility and priority of guidance over victory.
Two example verses are given: deferring to Allah's judgment.
3
Locate the key verse (16:125) and its three methods
Allah commands inviting with wisdom, good admonition, and arguing in the best way. Identify each method and its general aim.
Wisdom is knowledge and action, admonition is to motivate, best argument is for refutation.
4
Apply Ibn Taymiyya's classification to the verse
Ibn Taymiyya categorizes people into three: those who know and act (wisdom), those who know but don't act (admonition), those who deny (best argument). Match each method to the corresponding category.
This classification determines the appropriate approach for effective guidance.

المطلب الثاني : هدف الجدل القرآني
لم يكن الجدل في القرآن الكريم غاية تقصد في حد ذاتها، وإنما اعتبر وسيلة إلى تحقيق غاية أسمى وهي إقناع الناس بصحة العقيدة الإسلامية وضلال ما كانوا عليه من شرك ومذاهب منحرفة وكذا هدايتهم إلى الخير في السلوك بما يكفل لهم سعادة الدنيا والنجاة في الآخرة، فلم يكن الغرض من الجدل في القرآن الكريم هو مجرد إفحام الخصم وإلزامه وإبطال أقواله بل الأخذ بيد المجادل وإرشاده إلى الحقيقة وتوجيه نظره إلى حقائق الأشياء وما في الكون من عبر ودلائل على توحيد الله .
لذلك وجدنا القرآن الكريم يجادل خصومه من الكفار والمشركين وأهل الكتاب برفق، ولم يكن يمد في حبل الجدل إلى حد يقطع الألفة ويحمل على المزيد من التعنت والإعراض عن الحق، وكثيرا ما تختم آيات الجدال بمثل قوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّ اللَّهَ يَحْكُمُ بَيْنَهُمْ فِي مَا هُمْ فِيهِ يَخْتَلِفُونَ ﴾، وقوله : ﴿وَإِن جَدَلُوكَ فَقُلِ اللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ بِمَا تَعْمَلُونَ اللَّهُ يَحْكُمُ بَيْنَكُمْ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ فِيمَا كُنتُمْ فِيهِ تَخْتَلِفُونَ﴾
وقد دعا الله عز وجل في كتابه عباده المؤمنين إلى مجادلة خصومهم في العقيدة بالتي هي أحسن، فقال تعالى: ﴿ادْعُ إِلَى سَبِيلِ رَبِّكَ بِالْحِكْمَةِ وَالْمَوْعِظَةِ الْحَسَنَةِ وَجَدِلْهُم بِالَّتِي هِيَ أَحْسَنُ﴾ .
يقول الإمام ابن تيمية رحمه الله في تفسير هذه الآية : إن الإنسان له ثلاثة أحوال؛ إما أن يعرف الحق ويعمل به وإما أن يعرفه ولا يعمل به، وإما أن يجحده، فالأول هو الذي يدعى بالحكمة، فإن الحكمة هي العلم بالحق والعمل به.
The Second Section: The Purpose of Qur'anic Argument (jadal)
Jadal in the Noble Qur'an was not an end sought in itself, but rather it was considered a means to achieve a higher goal, namely convincing people of the correctness of the Islamic creed and the error of what they were upon of polytheism and deviant doctrines, as well as guiding them to good in behavior in a way that guarantees them happiness in this world and salvation in the Hereafter. So the purpose of jadal in the Noble Qur'an was not merely to confound the opponent and compel him and nullify his statements, but rather to take the disputant by the hand, guide him to the truth, and direct his sight to the realities of things and what is in the universe of lessons and proofs for the oneness of Allah.
Therefore we find the Noble Qur'an arguing with its opponents among the disbelievers, polytheists, and People of the Book with gentleness, and it did not extend the rope of argument to the point of severing familiarity and causing more obstinacy and turning away from the truth. Many times the verses of argument conclude with such statements as His saying: 'Indeed, Allah will judge between them concerning that over which they differ' and His saying: 'And if they argue with you, say: Allah is most knowing of what you do. Allah will judge between you on the Day of Resurrection concerning that over which you used to differ.'
And Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, has called upon His believing servants in His Book to argue with their opponents in creed in the best manner, He said: 'Invite to the way of your Lord with wisdom and good instruction, and argue with them in a way that is best.'
Imam Ibn Taymiyya, may Allah have mercy on him, says in interpretation of this verse: 'Indeed, a person has three states: either he knows the truth and acts upon it, or he knows it but does not act upon it, or he denies it. The first is the one who is invited with wisdom, for wisdom is knowledge of the truth and acting upon it.'
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage discusses the ultimate purpose of jadal in the Qur'an. The author begins by stating that jadal is not an end in itself but a means to a higher goal: convincing people of the truth of Islam and guiding them to right action. The goal is therefore educative and redemptive, not merely adversarial. This is reinforced by noting that the Qur'an argues gently and does not push debate to the point of breaking relationships. Two Qur'anic verses are cited to show how arguments often conclude by deferring judgment to Allah, indicating humility and avoidance of prolonged hostility. The author then quotes the famous verse from Surat al-Nahl (16:125) which commands believers to argue 'in the best way.' To explain this verse, Ibn Taymiyya's interpretation is introduced. Ibn Taymiyya classifies people into three categories: those who know and act on truth (invited with wisdom), those who know but do not act (invited with good admonition), and those who deny (invited with the best argument). The passage thus connects the purpose of jadal to a pedagogical and ethical approach, rooted in the Qur'anic paradigm. This section is typical of works on Islamic dialectic that emphasize the moral and spiritual dimensions of debate.

Key Terms
هدف الجدل
الحكمة
الموعظة الحسنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) With good admonition (maw'izah hasanah), to encourage action.
C) With the best argument (jadal ahsan), to refute their denial.
D) By leaving them alone, as they are already convinced.

Key Takeaway
Qur'anic jadal aims at guidance, not victory; the method of debate depends on the interlocutor's state of knowledge and action.

?

Purpose of Quranic Jadal: Guidance Over Refutation
Author explains the Quranic purpose of debate as guidance for truth, not just victory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Quranic purpose of jadal from mere refutation (ifḥām) and identify the three methods of daʿwa from Sūrat al-Naḥl.

Core Idea
Quranic jadal guides to truth, not victory.

This passage from a work on jadal explains that the Quran's method of debate is fundamentally constructive. The author contrasts the Quranic approach with mere refutation (ifḥām) and grounds this in key verses, including the famous āyah from Sūrat al-Naḥl that outlines three methods of invitation. As you read, focus on how the purpose of debate shifts from defeating an opponent to leading them toward truth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the stated purpose
Find the sentence where the author explicitly states what the purpose of Quranic debate is not and what it is. Note the contrast between 'merely confounding the opponent' and 'taking the debater by the hand to guide him to the truth.'
2
Contrast with ifḥām
The term ifḥām (silencing the opponent) is highlighted as a goal that is rejected. Look for how the author describes the Quran's approach as gentle and not aimed at cutting off familiarity. This shows the shift from adversarial to guidance-oriented debate.
3
Analyze the Quranic verses
Examine the three verses quoted: the first two end debates by referring judgement to Allah, and the third (16:125) commands debating 'with that which is best.' Consider how each verse exemplifies the guidance purpose rather than merely winning.
4
Apply to daʿwa methodology
The verse 16:125 classifies people into three categories (those who know and act, those who know but don't act, those who reject). Each category has a specific method: wisdom, good exhortation, and debating in the best way. This is a practical framework for anyone engaged in daʿwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجدل لهم سعادة الدنيا والنجاة في الآخرة، فلم يكن الغرض من الجدل في القرآن الكريم هو مجرد إفحام الخصم وإلزامه وإبطال أقواله بل الأخذ بيد المجادل وإرشاده إلى الحقيقة وتوجيه نظره إلى حقائق الأشياء وما في الكون من عبر ودلائل على توحيد الله. لذلك وجدنا القرآن الكريم يجادل خصومه من الكفار والمشركين وأهل الكتاب برفق، ولم يكن يمد في حبل الجدل إلى حد يقطع الألفة ويحمل على المزيد من التعنت والإعراض عن الحق، وكثيرا ما تختم آيات الجدال بمثل قوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّ اللَّهَ يَحْكُمُ بَيْنَهُمْ فِي مَا هُمْ فِيهِ يَخْتَلِفُونَ﴾، وقوله: ﴿وَإِن جَدَلُوكَ فَقُلِ اللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ بِمَا تَعْمَلُونَ اللَّهُ يَحْكُمُ بَيْنَكُمْ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ فِيمَا كُنتُمْ فِيهِ تَخْتَلِفُونَ﴾. وقد دعا الله عز وجل في كتابه عباده المؤمنين إلى مجادلة خصومهم في العقيدة بالتي هي أحسن، فقال تعالى: ﴿ادْعُ إِلَى سَبِيلِ رَبِّكَ بِالْحِكْمَةِ وَالْمَوْعِظَةِ الْحَسَنَةِ وَجَدِلْهُم بِالَّتِي هِيَ أَحْسَنُ﴾.
The debate (jadal) for them is the happiness of this world and salvation in the Hereafter. The purpose of debate in the Noble Quran was not merely to confound the opponent, oblige him, and nullify his statements, but rather to take the debater by the hand and guide him to the truth, directing his sight to the realities of things and the lessons and proofs in the universe for the oneness of Allah. Therefore, we find the Noble Quran debates its opponents from the disbelievers, polytheists, and People of the Book with gentleness, and it does not extend the rope of debate to the point of cutting off familiarity and leading to further obstinacy and turning away from the truth. Many times the verses of debate end with His statement, the Exalted: 'Indeed, Allah will judge between them concerning that over which they differ' (Surah Az-Zumar, 3), and His statement: 'And if they dispute with you, say, "Allah is most knowing of what you do. Allah will judge between you on the Day of Resurrection concerning that over which you used to differ."' (Surah Al-Hajj, 68-69). And Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, called in His Book His believing servants to debate their opponents in creed with that which is best, for He said, the Exalted: 'Invite to the way of your Lord with wisdom and good instruction, and debate them with that which is best.' (Surah An-Nahl, 125).
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage explains the true purpose of debate (jadal) in the Quran. The author begins by stating that the goal is not simply to defeat the opponent by exposing his errors or forcing him into a corner. Instead, the Quranic debate aims to guide the opponent to the truth, directing his attention to the realities of things and the evidence of Allah's oneness in the universe. The author then observes that the Quran deals with its opponents—disbelievers, polytheists, and People of the Book—with gentleness and does not prolong the debate to the point where it severs friendly relations and increases obstinacy. To illustrate this, the author quotes two Quranic verses that end debates by referring the matter to Allah's judgement, thus closing the argument peacefully. Finally, the author cites the well-known verse from Surah An-Nahl (16:125) which commands Muslims to invite others with wisdom and good instruction, and to debate only in the best manner. This verse classifies people into three categories (as elaborated by Ibn Taymiyya later): those who know the truth and act upon it (addressed with wisdom), those who know but do not act (addressed with good instruction), and those who reject (addressed with debate in the best way). The passage establishes that the Quranic method of debate is fundamentally constructive and aimed at guidance, not mere dialectical victory.

Ibn Taymiyya's Classification of Da'wah Recipients and the Role of Jadal
Ibn Taymiyya explains the Quranic verse classifying people into three categories for effective da'wah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify da'wah recipients into three states according to Ibn Taymiyya and explain why jadal is a secondary tool meant to repel opposition.

Core Idea
Jadal is a defensive response to opposition, not a proactive call.

Ibn Taymiyya's exegesis of Qur'an 16:125 provides a practical taxonomy for da'wah. He identifies three states of the addressee and prescribes a specific method for each. Crucially, jadal (debate) is reserved for those who oppose the truth, not as a primary invitation. This lesson will help you internalize this strategic classification and apply it in contemporary contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three states of the addressee
Ibn Taymiyya describes three states: knows truth and acts; knows truth but does not act; denies the truth. Write them down from the Arabic text.
These states determine the method of address.
2
Match each state to the prescribed method
For the first (knows + acts): wisdom (al-ḥikma). For the second (knows but does not act): good admonition (al-mawʿiẓa al-ḥasana). For the third (denies): debate (jadal).
Note that jadal is paired with the phrase 'with that which is best'.
3
Examine Ibn Taymiyya's definition of jadal
He says jadal is 'min bāb dafʿ al-muʿāraḍa' (from the category of repelling opposition). It is not an initial call but a response to opposition.
This contrasts with a view that debate is the primary method for all.
4
Understand why jadal must be done in the best manner
Jadal involves contention and anger (mudāfaʿa wa mughāḍaba). Therefore, it must be conducted with excellence ('bi-llatī hiya aḥsan') to repair the resistance it generates.
This condition ensures that debate remains constructive.
5
Connect to the overall Quranic purpose
The commentator concludes that Quranic dialectical methods aim to establish truths and remove doubts, not to argue for its own sake.
This reinforces the secondary, defensive nature of jadal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رحمه الله يقول الإمام ابن تيمية في تفسير هذه الآية : إن الإنسان له ثلاثة أحوال؛ إما أن يعرف الحق ويعمل به وإما أن يعرفه ولا يعمل به، وإما أن يجحده، فالأول هو الذي يدعى بالحكمة، فإن الحكمة هي العلم بالحق والعمل به، والثاني يوعظ بالموعظة الحسنة، فإن النفس لها أهواء تدعوها إلى خلاف الحق وإن عرفته فالناس يحتاجون إلى الموعظة الحسنة وإلى الحكمة، أما الجدل فلا يدعى به، بل هو من باب دفع المعارضة فإذا عارض الحق معارض جودل بالتي هي أحسن، وذلك لأن الجدال فيه مدافعة ومغاضبة، فيحتاج أن يكون بالتي هي أحسن حتى يصلح ما فيه من الممانعة والمدافعة. وهكذا يتبين أن ما سلكه القرآن من أساليب جدلية وما عرضه في ذلك أدلة من وحجج، لم يكن الغرض منه الجدل في حد ذاته مع المشركين وأهل الكتاب فحسب، وإنما كان ذلك كله لإثبات الحقائق في العقيدة والأحكام والإقناع بضرورة الإيمان بها وتصديقها مستخدمًا في ذلك ما يقربها به إلى العقول، حتى لا يكون موضع ارتياب لمرتاب، فهو يزيل الشكوك بالحقائق، ويبدد الأوهام والاعتقادات الخاطئة بالأدلة والبراهين.
May Allah have mercy on him. Imam Ibn Taymiyya says in interpretation of this verse: 'Indeed, a person has three states: either he knows the truth and acts upon it, or he knows it but does not act upon it, or he denies it. The first is the one to whom one calls with wisdom, for wisdom is knowledge of the truth and acting upon it. The second is exhorted with good admonition, for the soul has desires that call it to oppose the truth even if it knows it; people need good admonition and wisdom. As for debate, one does not initiate it; rather it is a matter of repelling opposition. So when an opposer opposes the truth, he is debated with that which is best. That is because debate involves contention and anger, so it needs to be in the best manner in order to rectify whatever resistance and contention is in it.' Thus it becomes clear that the Quranic methods of debate and the proofs and arguments it presents were not intended for debate itself with the polytheists and People of the Book alone, but rather all of that was for establishing the truths in creed and rulings, and convincing of the necessity of believing and affirming them, using that which brings them closer to the intellects, so that it is not a place of doubt for the doubter. It removes doubts with truths and dispels false notions and incorrect beliefs with proofs and evidences.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage presents the famous exegesis of Ibn Taymiyya on the verse 'Call to the way of your Lord with wisdom and good admonition, and debate them with that which is best' (An-Nahl 125). The author first quotes Ibn Taymiyya's classification of people into three states: those who know and act (addressed with wisdom), those who know but do not act (addressed with good admonition), and those who deny (addressed with debate in the best manner). Ibn Taymiyya emphasizes that debate is not a primary method; rather it is used only when someone opposes the truth. The nature of debate involves contention and anger, so it must be conducted with the best approach to repair the resistance it generates. After the quote, the author concludes that the Quran's dialectical methods, including the proofs and arguments, were not for the sake of debate itself but for establishing truths in creed and rulings, convincing people to believe, and removing doubts. The Quran uses arguments that are accessible to the intellects, dispelling doubts and false beliefs.

Key Terms
جدل
الحكمة
الموعظة الحسنة
من باب دفع المعارضة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, in what situation should jadal be used?
A) It should be used for all three types of people equally.
B) It should only be used when someone opposes the truth.
C) It is the primary method for calling Muslims who are negligent.
D) It should never be used in da'wah.

Key Takeaway
Jadal is not a primary da'wah tool but a defensive response to opposition, and it must be conducted with excellence to manage its inherent contention.

The Quranic Purpose of Dialectical Methods According to Ibn Taymiyya and the Commentator
Ibn Taymiyya explains the Quranic verse classifying people into three categories for effective da'wah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between debate as an end in itself and the Quranic use of dialectical methods to establish truth and remove doubts, based on the commentator's expansion of Ibn Taymiyya's view.

Core Idea
Quranic debate aims to establish truth, not to win arguments.

After quoting Ibn Taymiyya, the commentator offers a crucial conceptual clarification: the Quran's dialectical methods were never intended for mere argumentation. They were designed to establish truths in creed and rulings, convince people to believe, and eradicate doubts. This lesson will help you see the Quranic debates as truth-establishing tools rather than exercises in disputation.

Guided Path
1
Locate the commentator's conclusion
In the passage after Ibn Taymiyya's quote, the author says: 'Thus it becomes clear that the Quranic methods of debate... were not intended for debate itself... but for establishing the truths in creed and rulings.' Underline this sentence.
This is the key expansion.
2
Contrast with a possible misunderstanding
Some people think the Quran debates simply to argue or to defeat opponents. The commentator explicitly denies this: 'not for debate itself.'
The purpose is higher: truth-establishment and conviction.
3
Identify the means used
The Quran uses 'that which brings them closer to the intellects' and 'removes doubts with truths, dispels false notions with proofs.' These are educative, not confrontational.
The means are intellectual and persuasive.
4
Connect to Ibn Taymiyya's quote
Ibn Taymiyya emphasized that jadal is only for repelling opposition. The commentator extends this by explaining the ultimate goal of such dialectical exchanges in the Quran: they serve to confirm truth, not to engage in debate for its own sake.
The commentator is expanding the defensive role into a constructive purpose.

The Quran's Differentiated Approach to Jadal
Author categorises Quranic jadal by audience.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three main audiences of Quranic jadal and match them with their appropriate debate style.

Core Idea
The Quran tailors debate style to the audience's knowledge and state.

The Quran engages in debate (jadal) with various opponents, but it does not use a one-size-fits-all method. In this passage, the author explains how the Quran adapts its approach based on the audience's scientific and doctrinal condition. Let's explore the three categories: polytheists, People of the Book, and hypocrites.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three groups
Find the three groups mentioned: polytheists (mushrikūn), People of the Book (ahl al-kitāb), and hypocrites (munāfiqūn).
2
Note the debate style for each
For polytheists, the style is 'jadal hidāya wa-dalāla' (guidance and indication). For People of the Book, it is 'jadal takhṭi'a wa-ilzām' (refutation and obligation). For hypocrites, the style is severe with threats and warnings.
The passage explicitly states these differences.
3
Understand why the style differs
Polytheists are ignorant or misguided, so guidance is suitable. People of the Book have knowledge, so refutation and obligation are appropriate because they are not excused by ignorance. Hypocrites are inwardly opposed, requiring severity.
The author implies the reason: 'because they are knowledgeable' for People of the Book.
4
Recognise the overarching goal
The Quran's primary aim is supporting the Islamic creed, but the method varies to achieve the best result with each group.
The passage says: 'the important thing is the result while observing the specific style for each situation.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المهم في الجدل القرآني إذن هو النتيجة مع مراعاة الأسلوب الخاص بكل حالة، لذلك كان المظهر العام للجدل القرآني : معاملة الخصوم بما يتناسب مع أحوالهم العلمية والاعتقادية، فكثيرًا ما يكون جدل القرآن مع المشركين جدل هداية ودلالة، وقد يشتمل على تخطئة بعض مزاعمهم، بينما يكون جدل القرآن مع أهل الكتاب جدل تخطئة وإلزام لأنهم على علم، أما جدل القرآن فتبدو عليه سمات الشدة والقسوة مصحوبًا بالتهديد والوعيد. وهنا تجدر الإشارة إلى ميزة ذات أهمية بالغة في هذا الجدل القرآني وهي أن القرآن الكريم، على الرغم من أن الجدل فيه كان متجها أساسا إلى نصرة العقيدة الإسلامية في وجه المناوئين لها، إلا أن ذلك لم يكن مانعا من جريان هذا الجدل مع المنافقين على أساس متين من الموضوعية والعدل وإنصاف الخصوم والمناوئين. لقد وضع القرآن بذلك «أسس ما تؤكد عليه - اليوم - المناهج الحديثة مما يعرف بالموضوعية العلمية، حيث إنه أبان أن المناقشات والتحليلات لا يمكن أن
The important thing in Quranic debate, therefore, is the result while observing the specific style for each situation. Thus the general appearance of Quranic debate is: treating opponents in accordance with their scientific and doctrinal conditions. Often the Quran's debate with the polytheists is a debate of guidance and indication, and it may include refutation of some of their claims, while the Quran's debate with the People of the Book is a debate of refutation and obligation because they are knowledgeable. As for the Quran's debate [with others?], it shows traits of severity and harshness accompanied by threat and warning. And here it is worth noting a feature of great importance in this Quranic debate, which is that the Noble Quran, although its debate was primarily directed at supporting the Islamic creed against its opponents, that did not prevent this debate with the hypocrites from proceeding on a solid basis of objectivity, justice, and fairness to opponents and adversaries. The Quran thereby laid the foundations of what modern methodologies emphasize today, known as scientific objectivity, as it demonstrated that discussions and analyses cannot [be based on bias]...
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage analyses the three main audiences of Quranic jadal: polytheists (mushrikun), People of the Book (ahl al-kitab), and hypocrites (munafiqun). The author explains that the Quran adapts its style to the circumstances of each group. With polytheists, whose intellects are not guided, the debate is gentle and aims to guide and indicate the truth, though it may also include correction of their false claims. With the People of the Book, who possess knowledge, the debate is more confrontational, refuting their errors and obliging them to accept the truth because they are not excused by ignorance. With hypocrites, who are inwardly opposed but outwardly Muslim, the Quran adopts a severe style with threats and warnings. Despite the different approaches, the Quran maintains objectivity and fairness even with hypocrites. The author concludes by highlighting that the Quran established principles of scientific objectivity, as modern methodologies emphasize, by showing that discussions must avoid bias and treat opponents justly. The passage ends mid-sentence, indicating it is part of a larger discussion.

Key Terms
جدل هداية ودلالة
جدل تخطئة وإلزام
منافقون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) People of the Book
C) Hypocrites
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
The Quran adapts its debate method to the audience's knowledge and belief state, using guidance for the ignorant, refutation for the knowledgeable, and severity for the hypocrites.

The Quran's Commitment to Objectivity in Debate
Author highlights Quranic objectivity in debate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the principle of objectivity (al-mawḍūʿiyya) in Quranic jadal and explain how it applies even with hypocrites.

Core Idea
Quranic debate is both purposeful and objective, even towards enemies.

One might think that in defending the faith, the Quran would be biased or unfair to its opponents. However, the author emphasises that the Quran maintained objectivity, justice, and fairness even in debates with hypocrites. This section highlights how the Quran laid the foundation for what is now called 'scientific objectivity'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quran's primary goal in jadal
The primary goal is supporting the Islamic creed against opponents. The passage states: 'the debate was primarily directed at supporting the Islamic creed against its opponents.'
2
Note the surprising claim
Despite this goal, the Quran did not abandon objectivity. The author says 'that did not prevent this debate from proceeding on a solid basis of objectivity, justice, and fairness.'
3
Examine the example of hypocrites
Hypocrites are addressed severely, but even with them, the Quran maintains fairness. This shows that severity does not imply injustice.
The passage specifically mentions hypocrites as the group where objectivity is highlighted.
4
Connect to modern concept
The passage states that the Quran laid the foundations of 'scientific objectivity' that modern methodologies emphasize. This means that truth-seeking must be fair and unbiased.
The term 'scientific objectivity' is a modern equivalent, but the Quranic principle is earlier.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المهم في الجدل القرآني إذن هو النتيجة مع مراعاة الأسلوب الخاص بكل حالة، لذلك كان المظهر العام للجدل القرآني : معاملة الخصوم بما يتناسب مع أحوالهم العلمية والاعتقادية، فكثيرًا ما يكون جدل القرآن مع المشركين جدل هداية ودلالة، وقد يشتمل على تخطئة بعض مزاعمهم، بينما يكون جدل القرآن مع أهل الكتاب جدل تخطئة وإلزام لأنهم على علم، أما جدل القرآن فتبدو عليه سمات الشدة والقسوة مصحوبًا بالتهديد والوعيد. وهنا تجدر الإشارة إلى ميزة ذات أهمية بالغة في هذا الجدل القرآني وهي أن القرآن الكريم، على الرغم من أن الجدل فيه كان متجها أساسا إلى نصرة العقيدة الإسلامية في وجه المناوئين لها، إلا أن ذلك لم يكن مانعا من جريان هذا الجدل مع المنافقين على أساس متين من الموضوعية والعدل وإنصاف الخصوم والمناوئين. لقد وضع القرآن بذلك «أسس ما تؤكد عليه - اليوم - المناهج الحديثة مما يعرف بالموضوعية العلمية، حيث إنه أبان أن المناقشات والتحليلات لا يمكن أن
The important thing in Quranic debate, therefore, is the result while observing the specific style for each situation. Thus the general appearance of Quranic debate is: treating opponents in accordance with their scientific and doctrinal conditions. Often the Quran's debate with the polytheists is a debate of guidance and indication, and it may include refutation of some of their claims, while the Quran's debate with the People of the Book is a debate of refutation and obligation because they are knowledgeable. As for the Quran's debate [with others?], it shows traits of severity and harshness accompanied by threat and warning. And here it is worth noting a feature of great importance in this Quranic debate, which is that the Noble Quran, although its debate was primarily directed at supporting the Islamic creed against its opponents, that did not prevent this debate with the hypocrites from proceeding on a solid basis of objectivity, justice, and fairness to opponents and adversaries. The Quran thereby laid the foundations of what modern methodologies emphasize today, known as scientific objectivity, as it demonstrated that discussions and analyses cannot [be based on bias]...
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage analyses the three main audiences of Quranic jadal: polytheists (mushrikun), People of the Book (ahl al-kitab), and hypocrites (munafiqun). The author explains that the Quran adapts its style to the circumstances of each group. With polytheists, whose intellects are not guided, the debate is gentle and aims to guide and indicate the truth, though it may also include correction of their false claims. With the People of the Book, who possess knowledge, the debate is more confrontational, refuting their errors and obliging them to accept the truth because they are not excused by ignorance. With hypocrites, who are inwardly opposed but outwardly Muslim, the Quran adopts a severe style with threats and warnings. Despite the different approaches, the Quran maintains objectivity and fairness even with hypocrites. The author concludes by highlighting that the Quran established principles of scientific objectivity, as modern methodologies emphasize, by showing that discussions must avoid bias and treat opponents justly. The passage ends mid-sentence, indicating it is part of a larger discussion.

Ibn Taymiyya on the Purpose of Jadal in the Quran
Quotes Ibn Taymiyya on the purpose of jadal and explains its Quranic function.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Ibn Taymiyya's criteria for when jadal is permissible and how it differs from wisdom and good admonition, using Quranic examples.

Core Idea
Jadal is a defensive tool, not primary; it is only used when truth is opposed, and must be in the best way.

This lesson explores a key passage from Ibn Taymiyya on the role of dialectical argument (jadal) in the Quran. He distinguishes three methods: wisdom, good admonition, and jadal, each with its proper context. Understanding this distinction helps us see that the Quran's use of argument was not for its own sake but to firmly establish belief and remove doubts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three methods
From the passage, Ibn Taymiyya mentions three ways to invite to truth: wisdom (hikma), good admonition (al-maw'iza al-hasana), and jadal. Wisdom is for seekers, admonition for those needing gentle guidance, and jadal for opponents.
These are based on Quran 16:125.
2
Understand the condition for jadal
Jadal is only used when someone actively opposes the truth. It is not a primary method but a defensive one, meant to repel opposition.
Ibn Taymiyya says: 'As for jadal, it is not called for, but rather it is from the chapter of repelling opposition.'
3
Recognize the manner of jadal
Even when jadal is used, it must be done 'in the best way' (bi-llati hiya ahsan) because argumentation involves contention and must aim to correct rather than inflame.
The phrase 'with the best manner' comes from Quran 16:125 as well.
4
Analyze the ultimate goal
The Quran's argumentative methods were not for mere debate but to establish truths in creed and rulings, convince believers, and remove doubts. The goal is certainty, not victory.
Ibn Taymiyya emphasizes that all proofs aim to 'remove doubts with truths' and 'dispel false illusions.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
به، والثاني يوعظ بالموعظة الحسنة، فإن النفس لها أهواء تدعوها إلى خلاف الحق وإن عرفته فالناس يحتاجون إلى الموعظة الحسنة وإلى الحكمة، أما الجدل فلا يدعى به، بل هو من باب دفع المعارضة فإذا عارض الحق معارض جودل بالتي هي أحسن، وذلك لأن الجدال فيه مدافعة ومغاضبة، فيحتاج أن يكون بالتي هي أحسن حتى يصلح ما فيه من الممانعة والمدافعة (1). وهكذا يتبين أن ما سلكه القرآن من أساليب جدلية وما عرضه في ذلك أدلة وحجج، لم يكن الغرض منه الجدل في حد ذاته مع المشركين وأهل الكتاب فحسب، وإنما كان ذلك كله لإثبات الحقائق في العقيدة والأحكام والإقناع بضرورة الإيمان بها وتصديقها مستخدمًا في ذلك ما يقربها به إلى العقول، حتى لا يكون موضع ارتياب لمرتاب، فهو يزيل الشكوك بالحقائق، ويبدد الأوهام والاعتقادات الخاطئة بالأدلة والبراهين.
And the second is admonished with good admonition, for the soul has desires that call it to oppose the truth even if it knows it. So people need good admonition and wisdom. As for jadal, it is not called for, but rather it is from the chapter of repelling opposition. So when an opponent opposes the truth, he is argued with in the best way, because argumentation involves push and pull and contention, so it needs to be in the best way so that the obstruction and pushback in it can be rectified. Thus it becomes clear that what the Quran adopted of argumentative methods and presented of proofs and evidences was not intended for argumentation in itself with the polytheists and People of the Book only, but rather all of that was to establish the truths in creed and rulings and to convince of the necessity of believing in them and affirming them, using what brings them closer to minds, so that it is not a place of doubt for the doubter. It removes doubts with truths, and dispels false illusions and beliefs with proofs and evidences.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage presents a quote from Ibn Taymiyya on the nature of jadal, followed by an explanation of the Quranic approach. It begins by distinguishing three methods: wisdom, good admonition, and jadal. The first two are for those who seek truth or need gentle guidance. Jadal is only used when an opponent actively opposes the truth, and even then it must be done in the best manner because argumentation inherently involves conflict. The commentator then explains that the Quran's use of jadal was not for its own sake but to establish core beliefs and rulings, using rational arguments to remove doubts and false beliefs. The emphasis is on the goal of truth, not mere debate.

Key Takeaway
Jadal is a defensive tool for repelling opposition to truth, used only when necessary and always in the best manner, with the goal of establishing certainty.

Quranic Jadal Adapts to the Opponent
Describes how Quranic jadal adapts to the type of opponent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any Quranic jadal passage by identifying the opponent type and the corresponding jadal style (hidā'ī or takhṭi'a wa ilzām).

Core Idea
The Quran debates differently with polytheists, People of the Book, and hypocrites.

The Quran is not a monologue; it engages in debate (jadal) with various opponents. But it does not use a single approach. Understanding how the Quran tailors its argumentative style to the audience is crucial for interpreting many verses. In this lesson, you will learn the two main modes: guidance-oriented jadal and correction-obligation jadal, and when each is used.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponent
Look at the Quranic passage and determine if the addressees are polytheists (mushrikūn), People of the Book (ahl al-kitāb), or hypocrites (munāfiqūn). The opponent type sets the expected style.
2
Assess epistemological status
Polytheists are considered ignorant of true monotheism; People of the Book have prior knowledge (scripture) but deviate; hypocrites feign belief. This status determines whether the jadal aims to guide or to oblige.
3
Match opponent to jadal style
With ignorant polytheists, the Quran uses guidance jadal (hidā'ī), often gentle and focusing on proofs. With knowledgeable but deviant People of the Book, it uses correction jadal (takhṭi'a) and obligation (ilzām), i.e., refutation and compelling evidence. With hypocrites, harshness and threats appear.
This is a general pattern; some verses may combine styles.
4
Apply to a sample verse
For example, in Sūrat al-Baqarah, the debate with the Jews uses logical arguments and references to their own scripture (correction/obligation). In Sūrat al-An‘ām, the debate with polytheists uses observation of creation and reflection (guidance). Compare the tones.
5
Reflect on da‘wa strategy
This adaptation shows the Quran’s effective communication: meet the audience where they are epistemologically. A da‘ī can learn from this to choose appropriate argumentative methods.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المهم في الجدل القرآني إذن هو النتيجة مع مراعاة الأسلوب الخاص بكل حالة، لذلك كان المظهر العام للجدل القرآني : معاملة الخصوم بما يتناسب مع أحوالهم العلمية والاعتقادية، فكثيرًا ما يكون جدل القرآن مع المشركين جدل هداية ودلالة، وقد يشتمل على تخطئة بعض مزاعمهم، بينما يكون جدل القرآن مع أهل الكتاب جدل تخطئة وإلزام لأنهم على علم، أما جدل القرآن فتبدو عليه سمات الشدة والقسوة مصحوبًا بالتهديد والوعيد (2).
The important thing in Quranic jadal therefore is the result, taking into account the special style of each situation. Therefore the general appearance of Quranic jadal is: treating opponents according to their scientific and creedal conditions. Often the Quran's jadal with the polytheists is a jadal of guidance and indication, and it may include correction of some of their claims, while the Quran's jadal with the People of the Book is a jadal of correction and obligation because they have knowledge. As for the Quran's jadal, it shows traits of harshness and severity accompanied by threat and warning.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage outlines the principle of Quranic jadal: the method depends on the audience. With polytheists, the approach is guidance and gentle correction, as they lack prior knowledge. With the People of the Book, who have scripture, the approach is more forceful, correcting errors and holding them accountable. The passage also notes that when dealing with hypocrites, the Quran uses harsher language with threats. This shows a strategic adaptation for effectiveness.

Key Terms
الجدل الهدائي (al-jadal al-hidā'ī)
الجدل التخطئة والإلزام (al-jadal al-takhti'a wa al-ilzām)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Quran adapts its jadal style to the opponent's epistemological level: guidance for the ignorant, correction for the knowledgeable, and harshness for hypocrites.

Objectivity and Justice in Quranic Debate
Emphasizes the Quranic principle of objectivity and fairness even towards opponents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Quranic principles of objectivity and justice in debate and apply them to evaluate a real Islamic argument.

Core Idea
The Quran sets the gold standard for fair debate: objectivity even with opponents, and justice in speech, analysis, and conclusions.

This passage reveals a remarkable feature of Quranic jadal: despite being primarily aimed at defending the Islamic creed against opponents, the Quran maintains a rigorous standard of objectivity and justice. It not only sets this example but explicitly outlines the methodological foundations for fair argumentation, which are echoed in modern scientific methodologies. Let's unpack these principles and see how they can guide our own debates.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic claim about its own jadal
The passage states that the Quran's jadal was directed at supporting the creed, yet it did not prevent objectivity and justice even with hypocrites. Find the exact wording that establishes this balance.
The term 'objectivity' (الموضوعية) is a modern concept, but the passage applies it retroactively.
2
Extract the three types of justice mentioned
The passage lists 'justice in speech, justice in analyzing topics, and justice in deriving results'. Identify each one and think about what it requires in practice.
These correspond to different stages of argumentation: expression, analysis, and conclusion.
3
Link the Quranic methodology to modern scientific objectivity
The passage quotes a source that says the Quran laid the foundations for what is now called 'scientific objectivity'. How does the condition of 'freedom from backgrounds and enticements' relate to the Quranic approach?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهنا تجدر الإشارة إلى ميزة ذات أهمية بالغة في هذا الجدل القرآني وهي أن القرآن الكريم، على الرغم من أن الجدل فيه كان متجها أساسا إلى نصرة العقيدة الإسلامية في وجه المناوئين لها، إلا أن ذلك لم يكن مانعا من جريان هذا الجدل مع المنافقين على أساس متين من الموضوعية والعدل وإنصاف الخصوم والمناوئين . لقد وضع القرآن بذلك «أسس ما تؤكد عليه - اليوم - المناهج الحديثة مما يعرف بالموضوعية العلمية، حيث إنه أبان أن المناقشات والتحليلات لا يمكن أن تكون مجدية ومثمرة إلا إذا وقعت في جو من الحرية بعيد كل البعد عن ما فيها من خلفيات ودون اعتبار للبعديات وما فيها من إغراءات ومخادعات، حتى لا تكون المراعاة إلا لما يجب أن يراعى مما يكتسب قوته بما يقدم من أدلة عقلية وشواهد واقعية» (1). ثم إن القرآن بتوضيحه للجدل الهادف وبيانه لأساليبه، قد وضع للناس الخطة التي تمكنهم من معرفة كيف يصلون إلى العدل في القول، والعدل في تحليل الموضوعات والعدل في استمداد النتائج العادلة والمثمرة (2).
Here it is worth noting a characteristic of great importance in this Quranic jadal, which is that the Noble Quran, although its jadal was primarily directed to supporting the Islamic creed against its opponents, that did not prevent this jadal from proceeding with the hypocrites on a solid basis of objectivity, justice, and fairness to opponents and adversaries. By that, the Quran laid 'the foundations of what modern methodologies emphasize today known as scientific objectivity, as it showed that discussions and analyses cannot be fruitful and productive unless they occur in an atmosphere of freedom, far removed from backgrounds, without considering distances, and without enticements and deceptions, so that consideration is only for what should be considered, which derives its strength from the rational proofs and realistic evidence presented.' Then the Quran, by clarifying purposeful jadal and explaining its methods, has laid out for people the plan that enables them to know how to achieve justice in speech, justice in analyzing topics, and justice in deriving fair and productive results.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage highlights the Quran's commitment to objectivity and justice even in heated debate. Despite defending the Islamic creed, the Quran treats hypocrites fairly, setting a standard for modern scientific objectivity. The passage quotes an author (likely one of the references) stating that effective discussion requires freedom from biases and external pressures. The Quran thus provides a methodology for achieving justice in argumentation: justice in speech, analysis, and deriving conclusions. This shows that jadal in the Quran is not about winning but about reaching truth fairly.

Sabr wa Taqsim: Logical Enumeration in Jadal
Defines the method of sabr wa taqsim in Quranic jadal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the method of sabr wa taqsim to refute a claim by enumerating all possible attributes of a subject and showing none support the claim.

Core Idea
Sabr wa taqsim refutes claims by exhaustive enumeration, leaving no escape.

In Quranic argumentation, the arguer often faces claims that seem plausible but are actually baseless. The method of sabr wa taqsim (scrutiny and division) provides a systematic way to dismantle such claims. By exhaustively listing all possible attributes of the subject in question and demonstrating that none can justify the opponent's claim, the argument collapses. This technique is a hallmark of rigorous dialectic in Kalam and Usul al-Fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and claim
Determine the subject being argued about and the claim the opponent is making. For example, the subject is 'the Quran' and the claim is 'it is created'.
The claim must be something that can be evaluated by attributes of the subject.
2
Enumerate all possible attributes
List every plausible attribute that the subject could have. For the Quran, attributes might include 'eternal speech of Allah', 'temporally originated', 'composed of letters and sounds', etc. The enumeration must be exhaustive.
Exhaustiveness is key; missing an attribute could leave a loophole.
3
Show each attribute fails to support the claim
Go through each attribute and argue that it does not provide a basis for the opponent's claim. For each attribute, explain why it cannot justify the claim. For example, if the claim is 'the Quran is created', then the attribute 'eternal speech of Allah' contradicts creation, so it doesn't support the claim.
The arguer must show that no attribute can serve as a supporting reason.
4
Conclude the claim is invalid
Since all possible attributes have been examined and none support the claim, the claim is refuted. The opponent cannot salvage it by appealing to any other attribute because the enumeration was exhaustive.
This conclusion is based on logical necessity if the enumeration is truly complete.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أ - السبر والتقسيم : وهو أسلوب في الجدل يتخذه المجادل سبيلا لإبطال دعوى من يجادله، ويكون ذلك بحصر الأوصاف للموضوع الذي يجادل فيه ثم يبين أنه ليس في أحد هذه الأوصاف خاصية تسوغ قبول الدعوى فيه فتبطل دعوى الخصم عن طريق هذا الحصر المنطقي للموضوع.
A - Sabr wa taqsim: It is a method in jadal that the arguer takes as a way to invalidate the claim of the one he is arguing with. It is done by enumerating the attributes of the subject being argued about, then showing that none of these attributes have a characteristic that justifies accepting the claim in it. So the opponent's claim is invalidated through this logical enumeration of the subject.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage defines a specific Quranic argumentation technique: 'sabr wa taqsim' (scrutiny and division). It involves a thorough logical analysis: first, list all possible attributes or descriptions of the subject in question. Then, systematically demonstrate that none of these attributes can support the opponent's claim. By eliminating all possibilities, the claim is refuted. This method relies on exhaustive enumeration and is a powerful tool in dialectic, often used in kalam and usul al-fiqh. For example, in proving the impossibility of a second eternal being, one might divide attributes of necessary existence and show none apply to another entity.

Key Terms
السبر والتقسيم
الحصر المنطقي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the key step in sabr wa taqsim that leads to invalidating the opponent's claim?
A) Presenting a counter-claim with evidence
B) Enumerating all attributes of the subject and showing none support the claim
C) Appealing to a higher authority
D) Using emotional persuasion

Key Takeaway
Sabr wa taqsim is a rigorous dialectical method that refutes a claim by exhaustive enumeration and systematic elimination of all possible supporting attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Understanding al-Sabr wa al-Taqsim: Quranic Refutation by Enumeration
Definition and Quranic illustration of sabr wa taqsim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the method of al-sabr wa al-taqsim and apply it to analyze a Quranic argumentative passage.

Core Idea
Al-sabr wa al-taqsim refutes opponents by exhaustively enumerating and eliminating all possible causes for their claim.

This passage introduces a powerful dialectical tool used in the Quran: al-sabr wa al-taqsim (exhaustive enumeration and elimination). You will learn how to identify this method and see it applied to refute the polytheists' arbitrary prohibitions on livestock. By studying al-Suyuti's analysis, you will understand how logical enumeration can decisively invalidate an opponent's position.

Guided Path
1
Define the disputant's claim
Identify what the opponent asserts: e.g., 'Some male and some female animals are forbidden.' The claim must be specific enough to test.
In the example, the polytheists forbade certain male and female livestock without a consistent principle.
2
Enumerate all possible grounds for the claim
List every conceivable attribute or cause that could justify the claim. In the verses, the possibilities are: masculinity, femininity, womb-content, or a direct divine command.
The enumeration must be exhaustive to achieve certainty.
3
Eliminate each possibility by showing absurdity or falsehood
For each enumerated ground, demonstrate that it leads to a contradiction or is empirically false. For example, if the cause is masculinity, all males would be forbidden, contradicting their selective prohibition.
This step requires logical reasoning and knowledge of the subject matter.
4
Conclude the opponent's claim is invalid
After all possibilities are eliminated, the opponent has no rational basis for their claim; it must be false or arbitrary.
In the Quranic example, Allah concludes that the polytheists' prohibition is a lie and misguidance.

المطلب الثالث من مسالك الجدل القرآني : لقد جادل القرآن الكريم الخصوم، فأفحم المعاندين وألزم المنكرين وأرشد المترددين الشاكين وأقنعهم بالدليل القطعي بصحة ما يدعو إليه، وقد نهج القرآن في رده على الخصوم مناهج متعددة، وجادلهم بطرق متنوعة، مستخدمًا ذلك في أدلة كثيرة، منها : أ - السبر والتقسيم : وهو أسلوب في الجدل يتخذه المجادل سبيلا لإبطال دعوى من يجادله، ويكون ذلك بحصر الأوصاف للموضوع الذي يجادل فيه ثم يبين أنه ليس في أحد هذه الأوصاف خاصية تسوغ قبول الدعوى فيه فتبطل دعوى الخصم عن طريق هذا الحصر المنطقي للموضوع. وقد ذكر السيوطي رحمه الله في «الإتقان» أن من أمثلة هذا الأسلوب في القرآن قوله تعالى : (ثَمَانِيَةَ أَزْوَاجٍ ۖ مِّنَ الضَّأْنِ اثْنَيْنِ وَمِنَ الْمَعْزِ اثْنَيْنِ ۗ قُلْ آلذَّكَرَيْنِ حَرَّمَ أَمِ الْأُنثَيَيْنِ أَمَّا اشْتَمَلَتْ عَلَيْهِ أَرْحَامُ الْأُنثَيَيْنِ ۖ نَبِّئُونِي بِعِلْمٍ إِن كُنتُمْ صَادِقِينَ وَمِنَ الْإِبِلِ اثْنَيْنِ وَمِنَ الْبَقَرِ اثْنَيْنِ ۗ قُلْ آلذَّكَرَيْنِ حَرَّمَ أَمِ الْأُنثَيَيْنِ أَمَّا اشْتَمَلَتْ عَلَيْهِ أَرْحَامُ الْأُنثَيَيْنِ ۖ أَمْ كُنتُمْ شُهَدَاءَ إِذْ وَصَّاكُمُ اللَّهُ بِهَٰذَا ۚ فَمَنْ أَظْلَمُ مِمَّنِ افْتَرَىٰ عَلَى اللَّهِ كَذِبًا لِيُضِلَّ النَّاسَ بِغَيْرِ عِلْمٍ ۚ إِنَّ اللَّهَ لَا يَهْدِي الْقَوْمَ الظَّالِمِينَ) وقد بين السيوطي وجه هذا الأسلوب في هذه الآية الكريمة، فقال: إن الكفار لما حرموا ذكور الأنعام تارة وإناثها تارة أخرى، رد الله تعالى عليهم ذلك بطريق السبر والتقسيم، فقال : إن الخلق لله، خلق من كل زوج مما ذكر ذكرًا وأنثى، فمم جاء تحريم ما ذكرتم؟ أي ما علته؟ لا يخلو إما أن يكون من جهة الذكورة أو الأنوثة أو اشتمال الرحم لهما أو لا يدرى له علة أخذ ذلك عن الله تعالى، والأخذ عن الله تعالى إما بوحي أو إرسال رسول أو سماع كلامه ومشاهدة تلقي ذلك عنه، وهو معنى قوله تعالى : (أَمْ كُنتُمْ شُهَدَاءَ إِذْ وَصَّاكُمُ اللَّهُ بِهَٰذَا) فهذه وجوه التحريم لا تخرج عن واحد منها، والأول يلزم عليه أن يكون جميع الذكور حراما، والثاني يلزم عليه أن يكون جميع الإناث حراما، والثالث يلزم عليه تحريم الصنفين معا، فبطل ما فعلوه من تحريم بعض في حالة، وبعض في حالة أخرى، لأن العلة على ما ذكر تقتضي إطلاق التحريم، والأخذ عن الله بلا واسطة باطل ولم يدعوه، وبواسطة رسول كذلك لأنه لم يأت إليهم رسول قبل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، وإذا بطل جميع ذلك ثبت المدعى وهو أن ما قالوه افتراء على الله وضلال.
The third topic from the methods of Quranic dialectic: The Noble Quran argued with opponents, so it silenced the obstinate, compelled the deniers, guided the hesitant doubters, and convinced them with decisive proof of the truth of what it calls to. The Quran, in its refutation of opponents, followed multiple methods and argued with them in diverse ways, using that in many proofs, including: A - al-Sabr wa al-Taqsim (exhaustive enumeration and elimination): It is a method in dialectic that the disputant takes as a way to invalidate the claim of his opponent. This occurs by enumerating the attributes of the subject under debate, then showing that none of these attributes has a property that would justify accepting the claim, so the opponent's claim is invalidated through this logical enumeration of the subject. Al-Suyuti, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned in al-Itqan that among examples of this method in the Quran is the saying of the Most High: (Eight pairs: two of sheep and two of goats. Say: 'Has He forbidden the two males or the two females, or what the wombs of the two females contain? Inform me with knowledge, if you are truthful.' And two of camels and two of cattle. Say: 'Has He forbidden the two males or the two females, or what the wombs of the two females contain? Or were you witnesses when Allah enjoined upon you this?' So who is more unjust than one who invents a lie against Allah to mislead the people without knowledge? Indeed, Allah does not guide the wrongdoing people.) And al-Suyuti explained the face of this method in these noble verses, saying: When the disbelievers forbade the males of livestock sometimes and their females at other times, Allah the Most High refuted them by way of sabr and taqsim, saying: 'The creation belongs to Allah; He created from each pair mentioned both male and female. So from where came the prohibition of what you mentioned? That is, what is its cause? It is not free from being either on account of masculinity, femininity, the womb containing both, or they do not know a cause for it, taking that from Allah the Most High. And taking from Allah is either by revelation, sending a messenger, or hearing His speech and witnessing receiving that from Him. And that is the meaning of His saying: (Or were you witnesses when Allah enjoined upon you this?) So these are the aspects of prohibition, not going beyond one of them. The first necessitates that all males are forbidden; the second necessitates that all females are forbidden; the third necessitates that both types are forbidden together. So what they did of forbidding some in one case and some in another case is invalidated, because the cause as mentioned necessitates absolute prohibition. And taking from Allah without an intermediary is false and they did not claim it; and with a messenger similarly because no messenger came to them before the Prophet, peace be upon him. And when all that is invalidated, the claim is established: that what they said is a lie against Allah and misguidance.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage defines a key dialectical method called al-sabr wa al-taqsim (exhaustive enumeration and elimination) and illustrates it with a classical Quranic example from al-Suyuti's al-Itqan. The author first introduces the third topic of Quranic dialectical methods, noting that the Quran employed multiple methods of argumentation. The specific method is defined: a disputant enumerates all possible attributes or causes relevant to a subject and then demonstrates that none of them supports the opponent's claim, thereby refuting it. This is a form of reductio per enumerationem. The author then cites al-Suyuti's analysis of Surah al-An'am (6:143-144) where Allah refutes the polytheists' arbitrary prohibitions on livestock. Al-Suyuti explains that the polytheists forbade some male and some female animals without a consistent principle. Allah challenges them by asking: what is the cause of the prohibition? It must be either masculinity, femininity, the womb containing both, or a direct divine command. The first three lead to absurd consequences (all males or all females or both would be forbidden), which contradicts their selective prohibitions. The fourth possibility (direct divine command) is false because they did not receive revelation or a messenger. Thus all possible grounds are eliminated, proving their claim is a lie. This exemplifies sabr wa taqsim as an effective dialectical tool.

Key Takeaway
Al-sabr wa al-taqsim is a powerful dialectical method where exhaustively enumerating and eliminating all possible grounds for an opponent's claim leaves them with no rational support, thus decisively refuting them.
